Library
EXITS: NORTHEAST

SCORE 114/283; TURNS TAKEN 363
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 18/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Ah, the library of Montrose Mansion. You've heard of this place but the reality certainly fails to live up to its reputation. Where are the rows and rows of books covering every subject under the sun? Instead you see shelves which are mostly empty, books which look to have been thrown haphazardly around - some missing covers or spines or, in a few cases, everything in between as well - and a very bored looking librarian currently playing cards and yawning profusely. You don't even see any of the famed reading chairs purchased at great expense from abroad and shipped here at great personal expense. Instead, there's just a hard wooden bench on which the librarian is playing cards (meaning you don't even have a place to sit). Actually, you do see one chair, tucked away in the corner, but that's occupied by Bombur, no doubt still fuming from his argument with Scrimmage.  Tarquin is here, perusing some books.

> Examine books
Worthless as far as you can see. No great works here, no first editions or signed copies by respected authors, but instead the kind of cheap trash available off market stalls, jumble sales and second hand bookshops. During your previous career as a shelf-stacker in a bookshop, you encountered many of this kind.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 116.

> Ask Bombur about slave holdings
"The slave holdings, eh?" says Bombur. "Oh, I had always hoped that Monty would have disposed of them to ensure that knowledge of their existence did not fall into the wrong hands. Which, alas," he adds with a pointed look at you, "has now happened."

"You mean he kept slaves?" you say in your best 'oh-my-gosh! That's just terrible!' voice, complete with a hand to your mouth to display the correct level of dismay you're feeling.

"Unfortunately, I believe he did a few years back. He had money worries at the time and figured that acquiring slaves on the cheap and putting them to work as unpaid servants would save him a fortune. But... all it did was cause more problems."

> Ask Bombur about problems
"Namely," says Bombur, "that he fell in love."

"What's so bad about that?" you ask.

"With one of the slaves."

Ah. Yes, you can imagine that didn't go down well what with him being married to boot.

"Monty was head over heels in love with the poor girl. At first, he kept it on the quiet, worried that his wife would find out and take him to the cleaners, not to mention what damage it would do to his reputation - firstly for keeping slaves and secondly for sleeping with one of them! But, as is usually the case, the secret got out. Poor Monty feared he would be ruined."

> Ask Bombur about ruined
"Indeed - ruined! Now, a member of the nobility sleeping around is... well, not exactly nothing, but it's the kind of thing that happens with such regularity that it kind of loses its sting after a while. But sleeping with a slave? Now that is not the sort of thing that gets overlooked."

"What did Monty do?"

"Well..." Bombur rubs his hands together and grins. He really is the worst kind of gossip. "He freed the slaves and made it out that they had all been hired servants right from the start. It cost him a tidy sum in legal fees, of course, not to mention their wages on top of everything else, but the alternative was utter ruin, so Monty was only too willing to pay the price. Of course, what his wife thought about the situation is anyone's guess."

> Ask Bombur about wife
"What did his wife think about it?" you inquire innocently.

"Well, she wasn't best pleased but from what I gather there wasn't a lot of affection between them anyway. That her husband was sleeping around was probably of lesser concern to her than the scandal of him doing the dirty with a slave girl. The nobility are so very fond of their status after all." Bombur frowns. "You know, I'm not sure I remember what did transpire in the end. Sylvia, his wife (well, his second wife. The first, Constance, died in mysterious circumstances from what I hear), would know, of course, but I doubt she'd be willing to talk about it. Especially today of all days. Have you spoken to her yet? You should. I'm sure it'll be an illuminating conversation."

> Ask Bombur about Constance
"To be honest, I couldn't really tell you much about her. Have you asked Joves? Or maybe Lady Montrose? They'd know more."

> Give red button to Tarquin
"Hey, that's mine," says Tarquin. "Where'd you find it?"

"Under the bench on the patio."

"Great. Good of you to give it back to me."

You wait in case he's planning to offer you a reward.

But apparently not.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 118.

Very well done, too, though you say so yourself.

Kitchen

You don't even see much food being cooked. There's a large pile of it on a counter but it's still uncooked and no one seems to be in much of a hurry to change that situation.

Joves' Office
EXITS: SOUTHEAST

SCORE 119/283; TURNS TAKEN 386
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 19/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________You can't help but think that the office of the butler is very much like the man himself: cold, lifeless and utterly lacking in personality. Sure, it has the usual suspects - desk, drinks cabinet, files, boring painting on the wall next to an ancient bell - but done in such a way as if to suggest 'this is dull. Move along. Nothing to see here.' Joves is sat at his desk.

> Ask Joves about Constance
Joves gives you an evil look. Whether this means anything or if it is simply Joves being Joves, you can't say. "I have nothing to say to you about Constance."

"Really?" you say with a smirk. "I wonder what my good friend Sylvia would think about your attitude."

His look becomes even more evil. Almost... murderous. "I... see." You fancy you see the idea to murder you brutally and hide the body flit across his face. "Is that so? Very well, what do you want to know about Constance?"

You could ask him where Constance is, why she left Lord Montrose or what kind of person she was.

> Ask Joves about why
"Popular opinion is that they simply grew apart."

"And unpopular opinion?" you ask.

He scowls. "An affair, I believe. Though with who, or for how long, I do not know."

> Ask Joves about affair
"There are rumours, of course, but I am not going to speculate on whether there is any truth to them or not."

> Ask Joves about rumours
Joves scowls. "You think I'm going to satisfy your curiosity? Think again if you..." He trails off then smiles. It's not a friendly smile. It's the kind of smile given by a cat who has just cornered a mouse and is debating whether to eat it now or torment it for a while first. "Very well. Maybe we can come to an arrangement. You help me out and I'll tell you about the rumours."

"Help you out how?"

"Lord Montrose invited several people of low repute here tonight, and I had no choice but to make them feel welcome. However, following today's unfortunate events, I have no need to accommodate them any longer. Several have already been sent on their way, but a particularly loud-mouthed buffoon by the name of Hogg is still here and refusing to leave. Make him leave, by any means at your disposal, and we have a deal. I last saw him in the dining room."

Your score has increased by 1 point to 120.

Dining Room
EXITS: NORTH, EAST, WEST

SCORE 120/283; TURNS TAKEN 392
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 19/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________A large and overly-laden circular dining table occupies the middle of the floorspace in here, its strained legs fairly groaning under the weight of a feast that could probably wipe out world hunger in one fell swoop. A feast that is, alas, going to waste right now as news of the murder has somewhat dampened people's appetites. Hogg is by the table helping himself to anything and everything he can get his hands on.  A serving girl called Kristina is stood by the table, looking bored and not doing a very good job of hiding it.

> Ask Hogg about Joves
Hogg scowls. "That man, got the personality of a corpse and the charm of a rotting corpse." He spits. "Well you tell him I ain't leaving. Monty invited me and I ain't leaving till he asks me to leave."

"That might well be a problem on account of him being dead."

"Really? Not my problem. But..." He frowns. "Tell that old sourpuss I'll leave on one condition."

"Which is...?"

"I want the jewel Monty promised me after the party was over. Tell Joves that and see what he says."

> Ask Hogg about jewel
"It's mine by right anyway. Me and Monty were on a dig years ago and we found two items of great importance. I got one, Monty the other, and then when he was having money troubles a while back I lent him mine. When he invited me here tonight, he said he’d make sure I got it back. Well, he dies but that's no reason to welch on a debt. I want what's mine."

> Ask Hogg about dig
"Treasure, lass," he says with a laugh. "We was treasure hunters in our youth. Why, they even say Indiana Jones was based on me."

"Really? Who says that?"

He shrugs. "Oh, plenty of famous folk." He goes quiet, as if a sudden thought has just occurred to him. "Say, you don't think he'd bury it in the garden, do you? Ha! That'd be just like Monty it would. It'd be like recreating the dig when we first found the jewel."

"The gardens are massive," you say. "It'd take an age to search them!"

"You got a gardener, ain't you? Surely if anyone knows if there's buried treasure in the garden, it'd be him."

Your score has increased by 1 point to 121.

Ballroom

Dining Room
EXITS: NORTH, EAST, WEST

SCORE 124/283; TURNS TAKEN 436
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 19/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________A large and overly-laden circular dining table occupies the middle of the floorspace in here, its strained legs fairly groaning under the weight of a feast that could probably wipe out world hunger in one fell swoop. A feast that is, alas, going to waste right now as news of the murder has somewhat dampened people's appetites. Someone with more money than taste has hung several pieces of art on the far wall, none of it being to your fancy, framing a gothic archway while to the north is a large oak door.  Hogg is by the table helping himself to anything and everything he can get his hands on.  A serving girl called Kristina is stood by the table, looking bored and not doing a very good job of hiding it.

> N

Kitchen
EXITS: SOUTH, EAST, NORTHEAST, NORTHWEST

SCORE 124/283; TURNS TAKEN 437
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 19/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________You might have expected the kitchen to be a hectic affair with a chef shouting orders, frantic workers running back and forth and a dozen meals being prepared at any given time, especially considering the size of the mansion and the sheer number of people here, but instead you find a fairly small room, very quiet, with the chef sitting on a stool reading a book, a cat drinking spilt milk off a table and nothing much in the way of cooking going on. You don't even see much food being cooked. There's a large pile of it on a counter but it's still uncooked and no one seems to be in much of a hurry to change that situation.

> Ask chef about cake
“Cake?” he says, as if the very idea of cake on the day of a party is a bizarre one. “I think Lady Montrose had it all taken away.”

“Why?”

He sighs. “Not pink enough.”

EXITS: SOUTH

SCORE 124/283; TURNS TAKEN 446

________________________________Pink. These chambers are very pink. Incredibly pink. Exceedingly pink. Clearly, the owner of these chambers has a thing for the colour pink. There's the bed (pink), a bureau (also pink), a wardrobe (likewise pink), some fruit (they're probably meant to be oranges but, well, they're not) and a recliner (which, oddly enough, is blue) on which is lying none other than Lady Montrose herself. In a pink bathrobe.

> Ask Lady Montrose about cake

Evan's Room
EXITS: WEST

SCORE 124/283; TURNS TAKEN 450
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 19/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Judging from the state of his room, Evan is somewhat financially disadvantaged; in fact, even the woodlice and dust have given him a wide berth. He appears to have an interest in woodwork, with examples of his art on display in the window; other than that, and a seriously dilapidated wardrobe and a bed which leans badly to one side, his room is quite bare.  Evan is here.

> Ask Evan about cake
He looks nervous. “Of course I got rid of the cake… er, just as the lady ordered. I, er, wouldn't do otherwise.”

“So where is it?”

He looks even more nervous. “Have you had a good look through the gardens?"

"Why would the cake be in the gardens?"

"Er... er... because that's where I got rid of it. I’m, er, sure if you look hard enough, you'll find it in no time. Just check the whole gardens. And, er, don't rush things.”

________________________________Judging from the state of his room, Evan is somewhat financially disadvantaged; in fact, even the woodlice and dust have given him a wide berth. Evan is here.

> Ask Evan about cake
Evan at least has the decency to look embarrassed. “Er… didn't you find the cake then-“

“No, Evan, I did not," you say, trying to resist the urge to kick him where it hurts, "and do you know why I didn't find it? Because it wasn't there!”

“Um…”

“Where is it, Evan?” you ask, and make a point of cracking your knuckles as you do so.

Evan’s a good foot taller than you but he’s decidedly less vicious. Also, if you kick him where you’re intending, it'll hurt a lot more than if he kicked you in the same place. (Not that he will, of course. He’s a gentleman. You, on the other hand, graduated from the School of Dirty Fighting at a young age. You wouldn't know how to fight fair if you tried.) “I gave it to the chef to make a special cake for Sophia.”

Sophia. Of course. You should have seen that coming.

> Get pizza boxes

Your score has increased by 1 point to 134.

> Read journal
’Never expected to be sent here for work, but it seems like I don’t have much choice in the matter. Lord Montrose has been murdered in cold blood and they need the best man on the force handling it. Unfortunately, he wasn't free, nor was the second best man on the force. Or the third. Or… So they sent me.

It shouldn't be a difficult task to find the killer as none of these nobles have an ounce of common sense between them. They certainly don’t know enough about the nefarious craft of murder to fool a veteran of the force like myself!

To be fair, though, things haven't got off to the best start. None of the suspects really seem like obvious killers and I don't know what the motive behind the murder might be. And the men they've sent me are a bunch of incompetents! Aside from Bribeasy, none seem to have a clue what they're doing and he doesn't care for me. Probably thinks he should be in charge of the investigation just because he knows what he's doing or some nonsense like that!

Still, I should keep calm. The killer is bound to make a mistake sooner or later. I just need to be sure I'm around when he or she does."

Just as you suspected, Pinkerton is way out of his depth here and without your help, he'll never catch the killer.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 136.

> Examine desk

> Get ID card

Oh dear, he's awake. And he's looking right at you.

"Officer," he says, "what are you doing in my-" His eyes narrow as he gets a good look at you. "You!"

Knowing there's a time to explain things and a time to run, you run.

They all leave and once the coast is clear, you crawl out from under the bed and make a quick exit from the bedroom before Pinkerton or one of his cronies return and catch you.

There is a sinister lurking door to the southeast, and a doorway – minus a door – in the other direction, as if the architect had just had it with doors and decided one was enough.

> N

Ballroom
EXITS: SOUTH, EAST, NORTHWEST

SCORE 155/283; TURNS TAKEN 566
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________This happens to be the ballroom, an area normally of great laughter and jollity, but in light of the unfortunately-timed death of Lord Montrose, laughter and jollity seem to be in rather short supply. Previously happy guests are milling around like puppets with their strings cut, the happy-go-lucky music has ceased and if there is a cheerful countenance in the room, it’s hidden well away. The waiters have even stopped serving wine!

Of particular note is Lord Whatever (AKA the target of your affections), his pompous moustache even more ridiculous than usual, looking morose with nary a hint of his former ebullience to be seen.

There's the sound of someone being also slapped on the behind, a girlish shriek and then into the ballroom steps a familiar sight: Anton, one of the minor lords who is forever stopping by the mansion to see Lord Montrose. You've met him a few times before but you're not sure he knows what your face is like. Mostly, his attention is focused lower down.

"By damn, everyone looks morose today," he declares. "Who died?"

"Lord Montrose has been murdered," one of the serving girls says.

"Damn, that's a crying shame," Anton says to her chest. "Well, you'd better show me to the dining room so I can get a meal before the police want to question me. As you know, I am a very important person." In his mind, at least. "Lead the way."

"Er… I don't think the chef is cooking anything right now because of what happened."

"Really?" Anton says to her legs. "Well, I'm sure I can find something. Lead the way, girl."

With a sigh, the serving girl heads to the dining room. Anton, eyes locked firmly on her backside, follows closely behind.

Everyone in the dining room breathes an audible sigh of relief at his departure.

"What a positively ghastly man," says Lord Whatever. "Lusting after women half his age."

"Quite so, dear," you say to the pompous windbag, who clearly thinks you're really in love with him.

> E

Dining Room
EXITS: NORTH, EAST, WEST

SCORE 155/283; TURNS TAKEN 567
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________A large and overly-laden circular dining table occupies the middle of the floorspace in here, its strained legs fairly groaning under the weight of a feast that could probably wipe out world hunger in one fell swoop. A feast that is, alas, going to waste right now as news of the murder has somewhat dampened people's appetites. Someone with more money than taste has hung several pieces of art on the far wall, none of it being to your fancy, framing a gothic archway while to the north is a large oak door.  Anton is stood by the table, stuffing himself with pie.  A serving girl called Kristina is stood by the table, looking bored and not doing a very good job of hiding it.

> Talk to Anton
"Well, hello there," says Anton to your face while his eyes are checking out an area of you somewhat lower down. "I do hope the events of the day haven't been too stressful for you. If you need any help, you only have to ask."

Oh yes, the guy could give lessons to snakes on being slimy.

You could ask him for help (if you've no more common sense), ask about Lord Montrose, the murder or anything else you like.

> Ask Anton about the murder
"I have my suspicions about the identity of the killer, I can tell you but… well, let's just say I'll be speaking to the police at length about it later on. Why, with what I know," he adds with a wink, "I might be able to crack the whole case open for them."

> Ask Anton about his suspicions
"In good time, my dear. Suffice to say, what I know will likely lead to the villain's capture. Of course, if you really want to know more, feel free to meet me at that fountain in the gardens where we can talk in more… privacy. Just wait when you arrive there. I won't be long." He gives you a perfectly slimy smile. "Such matters should not be discussed where we can be overheard."

> W

Fountain
EXITS: SOUTHEAST, SOUTHWEST

SCORE 155/283; TURNS TAKEN 579
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________This exceedingly strange fountain appears to have been abandoned at the edge of the gardens; indeed, it's clogged with weeds and looks to have avoided a good cleaning for many a long year. Behind it, almost hidden from view by the overgrown weeds, is a building which, likewise, hasn't been cleaned for a long time. There's a sense of neglect hanging over both the fountain and the building and you get the distinct impression that they haven't been visited by any member of the cleaning staff in a long time.

> Wait
There's a rustling sound from the bushes and Anton steps into view.

"Ah, my dear," he says, "let us step into the den here. We don't want to be interrupted."

He heads into the nearby den. All perfectly innocent, you're sure.

> SE

Den
EXITS: NORTHWEST

SCORE 155/283; TURNS TAKEN 581
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________A lavish bar occupies one whole wall and looks to contain every beer known to man, and likely a few others as well. In the main area of the den is a large sofa set before a roaring oak fire and in the corner is a bed. It might be just your imagination, but you get the distinct impression that this isn't the kind of bed that sees much sleeping. It's the kind of bed used for... other activities.  Anton is sprawled on the sofa.

"Ah, welcome to my little home away from home," says Anton, waving a hand at the den. "It's been sound proofed in case you were wondering."

You really weren't but your stomach sinks about a foot when you hear that. The sound proofing is no doubt there so any torrid lovemaking can't be heard by anyone else in the mansion, but you imagine it will work just as well in the event of someone being murdered in here.

"Take a seat," Anton says, gesturing to the sofa. "We might as well get comfortable before we… talk."

> Sit on sofa
You sit down and Anton…

Anton…

… Anton says, "I'm glad you came because I really need to talk to someone."

What? He bought you here to… talk?

"Monty's death… has really hit me hard. He was like a father to me. I asked Jessica to meet me at the boat shed so we could talk but I think she must have gotten cold feet because she never showed up. Nice girl. Great in a bathing suit but… I think I need more than cheap, meaningless flings these days. I need commitment. I need…” and he looks at you as he says this “… a wife.”

Your stomach sinks. Sure, the reason you’re here in the first place is to bag yourself a rich husband - and Anton is certainly rich - but he’s also young, not very likely to die any time soon and any marriage to him is definitely not going to be as platonic as you’d like. And he’s got a roving eye so he’s definitely not someone you’re interested in. (You should know. You have a roving eye yourself and you’d hate to be in a relationship with you.) “Look," you say, "it’s very flattering that you think that way about me but we’ve only just met and-“

“I want you to find me a wife.”

“I, er - what?”

“A wife. It’s what is missing from my life right now. I’ve been thinking about it and it’s the right thing to do. And as luck would have it, today is the perfect time to do it.”

“It is?”

“Yes, with poor Monty - God rest his soul! - dead, his wife is once more free to marry again. Granted there’ll have to be a suitable period of mourning - a couple of days should suffice - and then we get married, honeymoon in the south of France and make love all day long. Sweet, sweet love. What do you say?”

“I say it’s the worst thing I’ve ever heard," you blurt out without thinking.

Fortunately for you, Anton’s tendency to ignore anything he doesn’t want to hear works in your favour this time. “Good. I want you to go and speak to her and gauge her opinions on the idea. It’d be best if she was on board, but I’m sure I’ll win her over one way or another. Well, what are you waiting for? I need to get in before any shameless cad tries his hand.”

> NW

Lady Montrose's Chambers
EXITS: SOUTH

SCORE 155/283; TURNS TAKEN 593
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Pink. These chambers are very pink. Incredibly pink. Exceedingly pink. Clearly, the owner of these chambers has a thing for the colour pink. There's the bed (pink), a bureau (also pink), a wardrobe (likewise pink), some fruit (they're probably meant to be oranges but, well, they're not) and a recliner (which, oddly enough, is blue) on which is lying none other than Lady Montrose herself. In a pink bathrobe.

> Ask Lady Montrose about Anton
Lady Montrose frowns. “Which one is Anton? Oh, it doesn’t matter really. Since my poor Monty was murdered, I’ve not been able to think of other men. Tell him no. For the time being, I’m not interested. And as far as he's concerned, I'll never be interested."

> Talk to Anton
Anton takes what you tell him surprisingly well. “Playing hard to get, is she? Good. I like a challenge. Okay, my plan to win her over is this: I gather she’s the kind of woman who’s drawn to a strong man so I’m going to put on a show for her. I’ll have someone be downright rude to one of the serving girls then I’ll step in and show the cad what’s what. When news gets back to Sylvia, she’ll see the kind of man I am and the rest will be history. The cad in question is that morose fellow who works in the art gallery. He owes me a favour. Tell him to head to the ballroom and I’ll send the serving girl I have in mind along shortly. If all goes to plan, I’ll be making love to my future wife by the end of the day.”

Doubtful in your opinion but you find yourself quite looking forward to Anton being taken down a peg or two.

Art Gallery
EXITS: NORTHWEST

SCORE 155/283; TURNS TAKEN 616
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Nothing screams filthy rich quite as loud as an art gallery in a mansion, mainly that it has an art gallery in the first place. This one isn't as capacious or ridiculously expensive as you might have expected, but it's still twice the size of your own apartment and has many, many exquisite works of art sealed away in glass cases. If you were an enterprising art thief, and had absolutely no scruples at all, you'd be fairly itching to make off with a few of the pieces from here.

Though hardly packed, the art gallery is certainly a lot busier than before you hung the banners in the lobby, with many of the nobility here browsing the works of art. Perhaps the oddest thing you can see in here is the circular door halfway up the east wall. It's 15 feet above the ground and has a grappling hook hanging from it. The remains of a smashed vase can be seen on the floor. Watching over the gallery, and fairly beaming with pride, is Carver, a man wholly transformed from when you first met him.

> Talk to Carver
Carver groans. “I was hoping Anton had forgotten I owed him a favour. Oh, very well, what do I have to do?”

You explain the plan to him.

“Sounds drab. It definitely needs pepping up if it's to have any chance of success. We need a bloodied knife to add some additional gravitas to the scene. Do you have one? No, well check the kitchen. They have plenty of knives there so I’m sure there must be one around with the requisite bloodstains on it.”

> Ask Carver about favour
He winces. "Embarrassing is what it is. A while ago, I made an inappropriate comment about Lady Montrose - I forgot what about exactly, but 'gold digger', 'cheap harlot' and 'shameless tart' featured heavily - and Anton spoke to Lord Montrose about it and arranged it so that I didn't lose my job. And ever since he did, he's let it be known that I owe him a favour."

Your score has increased by 1 point to 156.

> Give fake vase to Carver
He looks dumbstruck. "But… it looks just like the one that was broken. Better, in fact. Even though I know it's a fake, I'd be hard pressed to tell it's not the real thing." He puts the vase in the centre of the main display in the gallery where it fits in like it's always been there. "Ah, isn't it wonderful?"

You cough.

"Just wonderful," says Carver.

You cough again. Louder.

"Something wrong with your throat?"

"No, I'm *coughrewardcough* fine. Just *coughrewardcough* fine."

"That's a relief anyway. I'd here to see you come down with a nasty throat bug after your sterling work with the replacement vase."

"Don't *coughrewardcough* mention it."

Your score has increased by 1 point to 157.

> NW
Just as you're leaving the art gallery, you see a horrible sight: Pinkerton's face coming towards you! You have just enough time to duck to one side before he sees you.

"Where's this vase then?" he barks, looking around the art gallery as if he's never seen an art gallery before.

Carver points it out to him. "There? Isn't it won-"

"I've seen better." Pinkerton yawns. "Blimey, the lads went and had me put a stop to the investigation so I could come and have a look at it. I even had 'em stop the investigation so they could come in to see what all the fuss was. And you know what? I'm still wondering."

Shaking his head, Pinkerton departs. Carver watches him go then mutters, "ass. Some people just have no appreciation of works of true are."

"Or even realistic fakes," you say.

Carver glares at you.

> NW

________________________________You might have expected the kitchen to be a hectic affair with a chef shouting orders, frantic workers running back and forth and a dozen meals being prepared at any given time, especially considering the size of the mansion and the sheer number of people here, but instead you find a fairly small room, very quiet, with the chef sitting on a stool reading a book, a cat drinking spilt milk off a table and nothing much in the way of cooking going on. > Ask chef about knife

“Where do they get thrown out?”

Another strange look. The chef looks like he’s one question away from calling for the men in white coats to come and take you away. “Joves has Evan do it. Go ask him.”

Ballroom
EXITS: SOUTH, EAST, NORTHWEST

SCORE 159/283; TURNS TAKEN 655
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________This happens to be the ballroom, an area normally of great laughter and jollity, but in light of the unfortunately-timed death of Lord Montrose, laughter and jollity seem to be in rather short supply. Previously happy guests are milling around like puppets with their strings cut, the happy-go-lucky music has ceased and if there is a cheerful countenance in the room, it’s hidden well away. The waiters have even stopped serving wine!

Of particular note is Lord Whatever (AKA the target of your affections), his pompous moustache even more ridiculous than usual, looking morose with nary a hint of his former ebullience to be seen.

> Wait
No sooner have you started waiting than Carver enters. He's disguised but not very well: a cloak and a mask which make him look seriously dodgy. He makes a beeline for a serving girl called Louise and cries out, "Here, darling, grab this!" and takes a swing at her with the bloodied knife!

You were thinking that things had taken a rather unfortunate turn but at that moment, almost as if he waiting nearby, Anton appears out of nowhere and with a dramatic cry of "leave the lady alone, you bounder!" he tussles with Carver. The two struggle for a few moments but before anyone can step forward and ruin the scene - assuming anyone was planning to intervene, they all seem to be simply standing there gaping very ineffectually* - Carver gives a yelp of pain, drops the knife and flees through the door.

* Note to self: try and avoid getting attacked with this crowd as the only witnesses. You'll be long dead before any of them do more than say, "hey, do you think we should do something..."

Everyone cheers Anton, apparently believing this unlikely bit of ham acting to be genuine. Unbelievable!

"Never let it be said that Anton is a man without the guts to save a young woman from a lowly fiend," says Anton, sounding like he's prepared his lines beforehand. He even looks around after he finishes speaking to ensure that enough people have witnessed his act of bravery.

Louise throws herself into his arms and plants a kiss on his lips. Sadly, she seemed to believe it was genuine as well. You'd quite like to shake some common sense into her empty head but that would probably ruin things.

"Meet me back at the den," says Anton as he walks past you with Louise. "Went quite well, don't you think?"

"By criminy," says Lord Whatever. "I don't think I've ever witnessed such an act of selfless bravery in all my years."

Your score has increased by 2 points to 161.

Den

________________________________A lavish bar occupies one whole wall and looks to contain every beer known to man, and likely a few others as well. Anton is sprawled on the sofa.

Anton is pumping iron when you return to the den. Well, one small set of weights and they don't even look especially heavy but you guess it's a start.

"Sylvia strikes me as the kind of girl who goes for men with muscles," he explains, even though you didn't care enough to ask, "so I'm giving the guns a good workout. What do you think?"

What you think is probably unprintable but thankfully you're saved an answer by the sudden arrival of Louise. Minus clothes.

"My hero!" she cries and throws herself into Anton’s arms, knocking the weights to the floor.

For once, he seems lost for words. “Um…”

“We need to get married,” says Louise. “I've been giving it a lot of thought and I know it’s the best course of action. The way you jumped in and saved me from that brute… oh, Anton, you’re the one for me!”

Anton looks at her. The fact that she’s naked, and somewhat on the pretty side, is clearly a deciding factor. “I’d thought you’d never ask, babe,” he says, all thoughts of Lady Montrose fleeing from his mind. “Let’s head to the church right now!”

“Oh, let’s!”

And with that, the two of them depart the den. From the chorus of wolf-whistles that pursue them, you’re guessing Louise’s clothes haven’t shown up.

> Whistle
Barely have you whistled than Talia comes wandering along, as if she was just around the corner all the time.

"A locked greenhouse, eh?" she says. "Looks pretty easy to me. I'm surprised you needed my help at all. Why, the lock is barely even a professional model, more like some amateur thing you get people using because they look good rather than because they actually keep anyone out-"

"Can you open it or not?" you ask testily.

"Already done," she says, pulling the door open. "Still don't know why you needed my help, but we're now equal. Remember that, babe."

"Sure thing," you say as she walks away. "Babe."

Your score has increased by 1 point to 164.

Greenhouse
EXITS: WEST

SCORE 164/283; TURNS TAKEN 697
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Like most of what you've seen at Montrose Mansion, the greenhouse is overrun with weeds and well past its best. One wall leans badly to one side, the ceiling has taken a vacation and the floor creaks beneath in a way no floor should ever creak, especially one you're standing on. There's also a rank smell hanging in the air which reminds you uncomfortably of being a child and finding a dead raccoon had been living in the crawlspace beneath your house for a few months. The untidy jumble of rotting plants and sacks of weedkiller do little to help.

> Examine weeds
Straggly horrible things best avoided... ah, but what's this you see? Why, it looks like some very nice flowers dropped carelessly to the side of the weeds. Now, you're not the kind of girl who tends to care much for flowers, these are very nice indeed. And, as there's no one around to stop you, they're now yours.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 165.

> Examine smell
It seems to be coming from a pile of old leaves in one corner, which no doubt is best avoided. That smell is vile!

However, on the ground next to the pile, you see a red diode. What's a red diode, you might ask? Well, it's a kind of orchid and a very valuable one to boot. Hating to simply leave valuable orchids lying around where any unscrupulous thief could swipe it, you slip it into your pocket. Hey, it's doing more good in your pocket than it was on the floor, right?

Stables
EXITS: NORTHEAST

SCORE 168/283; TURNS TAKEN 713
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________As with most of the buildings on the Montrose grounds, the stables are remarkably rundown: most of the walls sag to one side, the floor audibly creaks underfoot and even the air has a neglected feel to it. The fact that only a single horse - a single ancient horse - is stabled here doesn't help either. As such, it's perhaps hardly surprising that there's a single hostler, called (of all things) Sally Dobbin, managing things, and as she's staring into space... well, it says it all really.

You hear footsteps from outside and into the stables walks Abrams. Clearly it was very warm on the walk over here as he seems to be exuding enough sweat to drown a small dog.

"Sally," he shouts (almost barks), "I 'as come to make you an 'onourable woman." He holds out the flowers to her. They're mostly dead now but you guess it's the thought which counts. "Will yous marry me?"

Sally looks horrified. You can't say you're surprised. "Marry you, but... but... dear me..." She rallies. "But I'm already married! To... um... Rex. Yes, that's it. Rex. That's a perfectly believable name, right? So... sorry, but I can't be married to two people at the same time, now can I?"

Abrams deflates. "Yeah, ah unnerstans comple'ly. Fine lass like you jus' 'ad to be married. Well, lass, if you ever gets tired o' that there hubby, or he dies like somewhat sudden, I'll be waitin'."

And with a long drawn-out sigh, Abrams departs.

Sally shakes her head sadly. "Oh, I do hope he doesn't my rejection poorly, but... well, did you see him?"

Coming from a woman who could give Black Beauty a run for its money in the pretty face department...

No, you're not going there. You'd better go and see how Abrams is handling his rejection.

> NE

"She were right impressed wi' me, I could tell," he says, clearly recalling a different version of events than the rest of the world. "Now... I just bides me time, waits for 'er gettin' bored o' her 'usband or 'im dyin' o' old age an' I got 'er."

"Um..." you say, which you feel adequately describes the situation.

"An' this be yer reward," Abrams goes on, handing over some oil which gives a faint this-is-going-to-burn-your-face-off vibe. "Don' say I doesn't pay me debts."

Well, you just hope Hogg is happy with the oil. It certainly took enough effort to get hold of it.

Hogg's Room
EXITS: SOUTHWEST

SCORE 171/283; TURNS TAKEN 727
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Technically this is a store room which someone - probably Joves - has converted into a makeshift guest room, though without the forethought to remove what was originally in here. So you have a very uncomfortable looking bed crammed in between all manner of boxes and crates and rolls of carpet. Added to this, there's a writing bureau by the side of the bed which is entirely too large for the room and, of all things, a rocking chair which was probably brand new around the time Hitler went mad and tried to conquer the world. All of this is overlooked by a giant stuffed bear (footnote 3). Don't ask. Seriously, just don't ask.  Hogg is by the rocking chair.

"Hogg!" you say. "You said you were leaving!"

He smirks and doesn't even look embarrassed at his outright deception. "I say lots of things, darling. Some of 'em are even true." He nods to the rocking chair. "Anyway, I'll be leaving soon enough but I ain't leaving me rocking chair here. Joves'd jump at the chance to throw it out with the trash."

> Give oil to Hogg
"Hey, you got it!" says Hogg. "Thanks, I won't forget this. Feel free to have a rock on my chair when you have the chance. It'll make a world of difference, I can tell you. For now, though, I'm outta here. I got my jewel back and my rocking chair is fixed, so I'm blowing this joint. Care to come with me for a wild night, doll?"

You mimic vomiting noises.

Hogg laughs and saunters out of his room.

Your score has increased by 3 points to 174.

> Sit in rocking chair
Now properly oiled, the rocking chair is almost silent as you sit upon it. And very comfortable. Almost too comfortable. You find yourself sinking into a deep sleep and struggle to resist as you’ve got far too much to do-

Too late. You’re asleep.

Muffled voices wake you.

“… don’t see anyone around. We should be okay to talk here,” says the first voice.

“Good,” says a second voice. “Right, I left the evidence there in his office for Pinkerton to find. Had to really. Left to his own devices, he’d probably be struggling to solve this thing for years.”

You look around. There are a couple of cops stood nearby, talking in low whispers, their backs to you. As of yet, they haven’t seen you in the rocking chair.

“What do you think he’ll do now?”

“Question everyone in the mansion would be my guess, find out who has an alibi and who doesn’t. It’s what he should have done in the first place really.”

The first cop shakes his head. “Really out of his depth, isn’t he?”

“He means well, though.”

The cops walk out of the room, still talking over their plan.

Ballroom
EXITS: SOUTH, EAST, NORTHWEST

SCORE 174/283; TURNS TAKEN 733
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________This happens to be the ballroom, an area normally of great laughter and jollity, but in light of the unfortunately-timed death of Lord Montrose, laughter and jollity seem to be in rather short supply. Previously happy guests are milling around like puppets with their strings cut, the happy-go-lucky music has ceased and if there is a cheerful countenance in the room, it’s hidden well away. The waiters have even stopped serving wine!

Of particular note is Lord Whatever (AKA the target of your affections), his pompous moustache even more ridiculous than usual, looking morose with nary a hint of his former ebullience to be seen.

Pinkerton and his cronies are gathered in the centre of the ballroom with the guests around them. You cross over and stand by Lord Whatever as a reminder that he's yours, and also so you can stand in his shadow so Pinkerton won't see you.

"Ladies and gentlemen," Pinkerton says. He's clearly in his element. "Today has been a terrible day as I'm sure we can all agree. But it is also a day that presents many possibilities, not the least of which is the apprehension of a particularly devious criminal, one who I have had many run-ins in the past and who, I firmly believe, is also responsible for the murder which has blighted this day's events."

You feel your stomach sink. He can't mean you can he?

Can he?

Pinkerton, clearly having a ball, goes on: "We have uncovered a crucial piece of evidence which will bring the identity of the killer to light. But first," he holds up a finger, "we need to speak to everyone at the mansion individually to establish their credentials and ensure their whereabouts at the time of the murder. We will use the annex over there," and he indicates a room to the north which you could swear wasn't there the last time you looked, "and interviews will commence immediately."

Several of the nobility kick up a fuss over this, but it's a kind of half-hearted kicking. One man point blank refuses to participate, but becomes quite a bit more helpful when several of the officers grab hold of him and frog-march him into the annex, while the rest of the nobility stand around looking worried.

"Have no fear, dear," says Lord Whatever. "We have nothing to hide."

He might not have but you certainly do. There's no way you're going to be able to avoid Pinkerton recognising you once he's questioning you in the annex. You need to act fast. Do you have anything that you might be able to disguise your features with? You once used a fake moustache to fool an eagle-eyed security guard. Shame you didn't keep hold of it.

Or is there another one somewhere in the mansion?

> N

Annex
EXITS: SOUTH, WEST

SCORE 174/283; TURNS TAKEN 734
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________The annex looks to be one of those rooms that has been ignored by people for so long that it's just given up on life and let things go. It's got a broken window that someone has (badly) tried to cover up with masking tape, a flickering bulb and a sagging table dividing the room in two. At this table, looking for all the world like he's only a small step away from ending it all due to sheer boredom, is a cop called Malarkey.

"Take a seat," says Malarkey.

You look around. "There are no seats."

"Oh." He gives the room a quick once over, then you, as if he suspects you might have hidden it. "Well, just APPROACH the table then so we can get this over with."

> Approach
"Nice moustache," Malarkey comments as you approach him.

"It's, uh, a problem in my family," you say smoothly. "All the women have hairy upper lips."

"Isn't it a fake moustache?" he asks, peering closely at you.

"I'm very embarrassed by my hairy upper lip, so I'll thank you to keep your opinions to yourself," you say, blushing furiously.

"Well anyway…" Malarkey asks where you were at the time of the murder - with Lord Whatever - who can verify that - Lord Whatever - and if you have any idea who might have committed the murder - not really - before thanking you for your time, advising you not to leave the country unexpectedly, and sending you on your way. All in all, that was quite a bit easier than you expected it to be.

Your score has increased by 3 points to 177.

You almost bump into Pinkerton as he strides into the lobby and just manage to duck back out of sight before he spots you. He seems stressed and you see him pace back and forth angrily before another cop hurries up to him in the lobby.

“How’d it go, boss?” the cop says. “We caught the killer?”

“No, no we did not,” says Pinkerton. “I was sure if we questioned all the guests we’d find something that stuck out as suspicious, but they all passed muster. The only dodgy guy was that fellow… I forget his name, but he's got a moustache you could lose your arm in. Reacted badly when Malarkey questioned him about the break-in last year, but that’s about it. What a waste of time.”

“Oh, don’t feel so bad, boss. Say, you want to go and arrest some folks for a laugh, lock ‘em in a cell overnight then let ‘em go in the morning? That always cheers you up.”

Pinkerton sighs. "It's good of you to try and cheer me up, but for now..."

These two fine upstanding members of the police force walk away, chatting.

Is that your future husband / bank account they're talking about there? Lord Whatever involved with a break-in? Surely not. He's way too square and boring - precisely why you're interested him, after all! All the same, you should probably go and ask him about it anyway. Just to be on the safe side.

“Hmmm…”

You experience a moment's unease at seeing Talia here talking to none other than Lord Whatever. You trust Lord Whatever - he's far too boring to be caught doing something as tawdry as cheating on you - but you could literally throw Talia further than you trust her. She's almost as dishonest as you.

"Babe!" you say to Lord Whatever and carefully sidle between the two of them, flashing Talia a smile which says, in no uncertain terms, that you'll claw her eyes out if she tries anything untoward with your future husband. She seems to get the hint because with one last look at Lord Whatever and his capacious bank account, she goes off to talk to someone else.

"A friend of yours or something, dear?" says Lord Whatever.

"Or something indeed," you murmur.

"She seems very, um, nice."

Not if you have any say in the matter.

> Ask Talia about Perkins
“Which one is Perkins?” she asks. “Is he the one who looks like he was dropped on his head as a baby or the one who has a face even his own mother couldn’t love? Either way, the answer’s no. I have standards.”

“You mean he’s not rich enough?”

“Exactly. Can’t you get that Sophia girl to go out with him? She looks dim enough not to realise what a bad idea it is.”

> Ask Jessica about Perkins
Louise sighs. “Let me guess, you asked everyone else and they all said no? Figures. You sleep around with every guy who’ll give you the time of day and people think you’re easy. Well, I want something in return.”

“You get to go out with Perkins, isn’t that reward enough?” you ask hopefully.

She gives you a very disappointed look. “Oh, please. No, what I want is a priceless orchid - the red diode. It’s been kept in the greenhouse for ages but I can't fetch it myself because Joves has me working here and he'll become suspicious if I suddenly disappear. You'll have to fetch it for me."

> Give red diode to Jessica
She looks surprised as if she expected you to die a horrible death. “I’m surprised,” she says, “I really expected you to die a horrible death. But, oh my diode. Isn't it beautiful?”

“You’re a big fan of exotic flowers?”

She snorts. “Hardly! But do you know what this baby sells for on eBay? I'll make a killing.” Then she sighs. “A deal’s a deal. I’d better go and get ready for my date with Podkins.”

“Perkins."

“Whatever.”

Clutching her priceless-on-eBay red diode, she departs.

Perkins' Room

SCORE 178/283; TURNS TAKEN 809

________________________________Very few rooms in the mansion could ever be considered ‘charming’ or ‘homely’ and this one is no exception. “Not quite,” you say, “but I got a very nice girl called Jessica to go out with you.” And bribed her to boot.

“Jessica?" He frowns. "Which one is she? She’d better be hot ‘cos it'll ruin my street cred if I’m seen around town with an ugly girl.”

And just imagine what it'll do to Jessica‘s street cred when she’s seen around town with Perkins. Poor girl will be a social outcast. “Don’t worry, I don’t think you'll have any issue with her looks.” Her with your looks however… “Now, about this deed I need signing…”

“Yeah, yeah,” he mutters, attention already on Jessica. He scribbles his name on the deed. “Now, I got a date.”

With that, he hurries from the room. You offer up a prayer for poor Jessica but reflect that at least you got what you came for.

________________________________This exceedingly strange fountain appears to have been abandoned at the edge of the gardens; indeed, it's clogged with weeds and looks to have avoided a good cleaning for many a long year. Behind it, almost hidden from view by the overgrown weeds, is a building which, likewise, hasn't been cleaned for a long time. There's a sense of neglect hanging over both the fountain and the building and you get the distinct impression that they haven't been visited by any member of the cleaning staff in a long time.

Satan strides imperiously into sight. “The deed? Tell me you got it signed so I’m not forced to reside with that lovesick dope Evan.”

You hand the signed deed over. "All taken care of."

“Ah, excellent.” Satan rolls the deed up and slips it into his pocket. “I’m sure that was a task which a small child could have accomplished with ease, but I still wondered if it might not be a little beyond you. It’s good to see that you've managed to exceed my exceedingly low expectations for you. And now,” he adds, with a clap, “to my room.”

“Don’t worry about a reward,” you call after him, and to your complete lack of surprise, Satan does not stop.

Perkins' Room
EXITS: SOUTHWEST

SCORE 181/283; TURNS TAKEN 833
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Very few rooms in the mansion could ever be considered ‘charming’ or ‘homely’ and this one is no exception. What it lacks in charming and homely, however, it more than makes up for with a chilling draft and a window which could be deemed as both open and closed at the same time. Other than this, there’s the bed - at least you assume it’s a bed but you’re willing to admit you could be wrong - and something that might be a beer cooler, if it wasn't placed right next to an open log fire.

Technically you guess this is now Satan's room and not Perkins' room but whoever handles the updates for this of thing is clearly slacking. The man in question is stood nearby, looking not very impressed with his new accommodation.

"Ah, it's you," says Satan. You can't help but notice how he seems less than thrilled. "Well, at least you're moderately useful, I guess. That's something." He stares at you. "And you're still here. What a drag."

> Talk to Satan
"Oh, how droll," he says. "Dazzle me with your wit, why don't you?"

You could ask him about himself, Joves, the murder, what's the deal with him and Sally, the break-in or anything else you like.

> Ask Satan about himself
"Believe me, there's nothing about me that I'm going to discuss with you. I am, after all, a mere servant here at the mansion."

> Ask Satan about servant
"Yes, a servant. Nothing more, nothing less." He looks thoughtful for a moment. "I remember the first day I started here, me and Emma. Happy days."

> Ask Satan about Emma
You see a brief crack in Satan's icy facade when you mention Emma, though it is masked very quickly. "That silly serving girl? No, don't waste my time with her. She's beneath me and needs to find someone more suited to her intellectually. A frog, perhaps. No, do not ask me about her again. Never again. I do not wish to answer any more questions about her."

From the way he's going on, you get the distinct impression that he wants you to ask him about Emma again.

> Ask Satan about Emma
Satan grimaces, though you get the distinct impression that he's quite pleased you asked him again. "Ours was a relationship doomed from the word go. I am clever, she is simple; I am interested in the finer things in life, she shops at the co-op; I listen to Bach and nothing else, she likes Harry Styles… but there was an attraction there. I think it may have something to do with the fact that she is remarkably attractive and has a fondness for skinny dipping, but I could be wrong. Alas, it wasn't to be. My father, who I've never got on with well at the best of times, has forbid us from seeing each other and while I'm quite prepared to ignore him and damn the consequences, she is not. I believe she will leave and that will be the end of the matter. Unless," he adds with a look at you, "someone would act as an intermediary between us to facilitate an arrangement whereby we see each other and keep my father blissfully unaware. Ask me about my plan if you're interested. Needless to say, there will be a reward."

> Ask Satan about plan
"Excellent." Satan rubs his hands together in the kind of way you imagine his namesake might do. "The first part of my plan involves seeing Emma fired."

You frown. "How is that going to help?"

"Simple. It will remove Emma from my father's sight. Out of sight is indeed out of mind. Once she is no longer around, he will forget all about her and we can be together. This needs to be done with some subterfuge. Only my father can fire her but thankfully due to the sheer volume of people he fires, acquiring an employee dismissal form should be an easy matter. Go to his room and find one, then return it to me and I can alter it to read Emma's name."

> Give form to Satan
"Yes, this should suffice. Now, some artful forgery…" He takes a pen out and writes Emma's name on the form. "Perfect! Take it to my father, get him to stamp it, and Emma is gone. And I am free to court her without my father interfering."

"Won't he get suspicious if I just hand him this form? And why would he fire her just because her name is on the form?"

Satan sighs. "It's the way his mind works," he explains, as if he is talking to a small child or someone who is a little slow. "If Emma's name is on the form, it must be correct because only he has the right to put names there for dismissal, and as only he has the right then he must have had good reason for putting it there because he is perfect and not capable of making mistakes. He will stamp it, believe me. I would bet your very life on it."

Your score has increased by 1 point to 182.

"What do you mean - you got me fired?!?" Emma is shouting. "I have debts. I have loan sharks after me! If I can't pay my debts, they'll break my knees!"

"Yes, dear, it was all down to me," says Satan, who clearly needs a few lessons in when to keep his mouth shut. "Now you can get out from under my father's grip and be a free woman. And don't worry," he adds, "I'll still love you with broken knees."

"But… but…" Emma throws up her hands in dismay. "I've got to go… maybe if I get a good head start the loan sharks won't be able to find me to break anything…"

She runs from the room, leaving Satan stood there, looking remarkably confused.

"Women," he says, "I'll never understand them. You hatch a marvelous plan to get them fired so you can date them without your father's interference and all they can think about is getting their knees broken." He sighs deeply. "Some people."

With a shake of his head, he wanders out of the room. Your muttered "hey, seriously, where's my damn reward?" falls on deaf ears.

> Ask Satan about Silas
"Silas? That incompetent reprobate? What's he been up to now?"

You explain about the harassment Silas has been conducting against Joves.

Which causes Satan to burst out laughing! (To be fair, it's not very good laughing, as if Satan hasn't had much practice in the past, and comes across sounding about as humorous as a death rattle, but it's nevertheless laughter from someone who you never expected to see doing it.)

"I shouldn't laugh," says Satan, wiping tears from his eyes, "but there's little love beneath myself and my father and finding out that Silas - of all people - has been harassing him quite makes my day."

“What can you tell me about Silas?”

“He’s a fool, I can tell you that. He thinks he’s some kind of revolutionary, standing up for the oppressed masses here at the mansion and trying to save them from a life of slavery… while at the same time quietly overlooking the fact that they just work here, they aren't slaves and his acts of ‘heroism’ - as he calls them - just make the whole situation worse. I hear he’s been hiding out in the east wing after my father tried to grab him, but daddy dearest doesn't know about the false panel in the fireplace where Silas is hiding so I doubt he’s been caught yet.” He laughs. "Oh yes, I know lots of things like that which my father is wilfully ignorant of."

Interesting. If you can find the panel yourself, you might be able to get the drop on Silas. What use he will be is debatable, but you feel you should definitely speak to him at some point.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 187.

Silas' Lair
EXITS: SOUTHEAST

SCORE 191/283; TURNS TAKEN 880
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 20/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________No, that isn't the name you'd have given this place, but instead the name someone has written on a sign jammed into a crack in the wall. The 'lair' consists of a scruffy sleeping bag (yes, it's seen better years, unless it was designed to be tatty on purpose), a stack of old novels and a large amount of dust (though to be fair this was unlikely to have been a design choice but more the kind of thing that just happens). An ancient piece of scaffolding props up one wall, and you just hope it's a lot sturdier than it looks, because if it gives way you'll probably end up buried.  Silas is here.

Even before you reached this room - this (heh heh) lair - you could hear the bizarre sound of someone dancing around in what you now see as an embarrassing display of ninja moves performed by someone who clearly has no idea how they're really done. The someone in question - Silas, you're guessing - is wearing a mask which looks like the sort of thing you could pick up at a jumble sale.

"Silas!" you call and the cloaked figure spins around, yelps and falls over on its ass. Overall, this is very anti-climatic after the effort you went to in order to track him down.

"Leave me alone!" Silas yelps. "I ain't done nothing wrong."

Whoever told him he could move like a ninja would probably disagree, but you could ask him about himself, the murder, Lord Montrose, his disguise (such as it is) or anything else you like.

> Get mask
You grab at the mask, but Silas gives a high-pitched girlish shriek and backs away hurriedly.

"Unhand me, varlet!" he cries and then there's a sudden flash and a cloud of smoke and he is gone.

Waving your hands to disperse the effects of the smoke bomb, you have a quick look around the room to see if you can spot where he went. Alas not, but you do find something he left behind.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 192.

Part of you is even tempted to go back to a previous life and see if it was there all along, but no… that'd be silly.

Graveyard
EXITS: NORTHWEST

SCORE 196/283; TURNS TAKEN 916
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 21/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________It's weird how the ground here is covered in thick mist that for some reason hasn't spread to the rest of the mansion grounds despite the fact that there's nothing to stop it doing so. It also seems much darker here than in the nearby parking lot, not to mention a lot colder. Now, while the graveyard isn't very large, you see a veritable horde of gravestones, and a rather chilling open grave. Also, the solitary tree with seriously scary looking branches shaped like clutching fingers really doesn't do any wonders for this place's creepy ambience.

> Examine graveyard
Creepy and then some. It almost looks like this location has somehow found its way here from another game...

No wonder your apprentice grave digging job never went anywhere. This place is just unsettling.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 198.

> Examine mist
It really is bizarre how the mist clings to the graveyard and doesn't simply float into the car park. If you didn't know better, you'd swear it wasn't real mist at all but some kind of fake mist like you get on stage (something you've encountered a time or two before in your former career as an aspiring stage actress).

Your score has increased by 2 points to 200.

> Examine open grave
You half-expect to see a dead body in the bottom of the grave - or even a flesh-eating zombie considering how creepy the graveyard is - so it's quite a relief to see that it's nothing more sinister than just an empty hole in the ground.

"Hey, get away from me hole!" someone shouts and a spotty-faced youth runs into the graveyard, waving a stick around in a manner he probably thinks is threatening. (He's wrong.) "Only registered gravediggers is allowed to mess wiv the holes!”

“And who might you be?” you ask.

He puffs up his chest to try and look intimidating. (He fails. He’s smaller than you and you’re hardly known for being abnormally tall.) “I’m Rufus. They call me, er, Rufus the Ripper.” You doubt anyone has ever called him Rufus the Ripper. “And I’m the chief gravedigger ‘round these parts and what I say goes. Everyone knows that.” Yeah. Right. “You’s trespassing so you’d better get going before I make you regret ever being born.”

Oh brother…

Assuming you’re not wasting your time, you could ask him about himself, the murder, the graveyard, Old Man Watson or anything else you like.

> Ask Rufus about Old Man Watson
“Former grave digger,” says Rufus sadly, “taught me everything I know about digging graves.” He stumbles and almost falls into a grave as he says this. It appears to be on the verge of collapsing. “Now sadly gone to the great graveyard in the sky. Or, actually this one as he’s buried right over there. They all loved him, they did. Even Joves, and that man don’t love anyone. Why, d’you know they gave him a special seal ‘cos of his service?”

“Do you know what happened to the seal?” you ask.

“I think his son stole it.”

“His son?”

“Silas.”

Interesting. So Silas is Old Man Watson’s son. You aren’t sure what this means, but you have a sneaking suspicion it has something to do with the events of the day. Clearly you need to find Silas again and see what else he knows.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 201.

Lobby
EXITS: SOUTH, EAST, NORTHWEST, UP

SCORE 201/283; TURNS TAKEN 923
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 23/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________The lobby of Montrose Mansion is not quite as chaotic as when you first arrived, due to the absence of the assembled clucking nobility who have been moved on by the police. A route is now visible to the south, which leads outside to the gardens, and there is a previously hidden corridor to the east. And there's a rather large statue of Lord Montrose overlooking the lobby, which you're sure must have been visible before but you don't remember seeing any sign of it. The overly large ego of some noble no doubt hid it from view. Oh, and there are some banners advertising the appeals of the art gallery hanging from the stairs. Very well done, too, though you say so yourself.

There’s a kerfuffle in the lobby as you return to the mansion: Evan is being led down the stairs, handcuffed, by several beefy officers while Pinkerton watches on with a satisfied look on his face.

“But I didn’t do it!” Evan is protesting. “I’m no killer!”

“Tell that to the firing squad,” says Pinkerton. “You’re guilty, Evan, and I’ll see you hang and shot for this.”

“They don’t hang people in England,” says Joves, striding into the lobby. “Or shoot them for that matter. What is the meaning of this?”

“New evidence,” says Pinkerton. “It all points to Evan being the guilty party.”

“Him?” Joves looks at Evan and scowls. “The man’s an incompetent buffoon who's barely capable of cleaning without causing a disaster. I hardly think he’s got the wherewithal to commit a complex murder.”

“Evidence is evidence, pal.” Pinkerton turns to his men. “Put him in the cells we found near the annex while we investigate further. Something tells me this is going to be over soon.”

The police drag Evan away, and Joves, after a pointed look at Pinkerton, then at you, returns to his office. Calm descends on the lobby.

Joves' Office
EXITS: SOUTHEAST

SCORE 201/283; TURNS TAKEN 928
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 23/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________You can't help but think that the office of the butler is very much like the man himself: cold, lifeless and utterly lacking in personality. Sure, it has the usual suspects - desk, drinks cabinet, files, boring painting on the wall next to an ancient bell - but done in such a way as if to suggest 'this is dull. Move along. Nothing to see here.' Joves is sat at his desk.

“Did you witness that farce?” Joves snaps the moment you walk into his office. “Evan - a killer? The man is so incompetent, he’d stab himself to death before he harmed anyone else. Now the police have arrested him and will no doubt put a stop to their investigation so the real murderer will go free. This simply won't do! Also, I just paid Evan and I'm not having him loafing off in custody when there's work to be done.”

“What can we do?”

“We need to ensure the investigation stays open for a start, which means we need to find out what evidence they have on Evan and disprove it. If you pose as his legal council, you should be able to trick them into letting you in to see him. Considering how morbidly stupid they all seem, all you’ll need are some glasses, a briefcase, a cravat and a legal pad. I take it you have them to hand?”

“Er…”

“Once you do, head to the annex and see what you can find out.”

"Hang on! And where am I supposed to find them?"

"You surely don't need my help finding all of them, do you?" He sighs. "Very well. Ask me about each of them separately if you're really incapable of finding anything for yourself."

> Ask Joves about legal pad
"My son Satan probably has one lying around. He wanted to be a lawyer at one stage."

Cells
EXITS: EAST

SCORE 205/283; TURNS TAKEN 939
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 23/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Who knew there were cells at Montrose Mansion? Not you, but then that’s just where you are right now: a series of ancient stone cells with metal bars thrust into the ground. All but one of the cells is empty and in that one is Evan, looking even more stressed than you've seen him. A cop by the name of Sherlock is standing guard here to ensure no escape attempts are made but, as his attention is wholly focused on the magazine in his hand, you should be fine.  Evan is here.

At your arrival, Sherlock looks up, looks you up and down in a way which will earn him a hard kick in the crown jewels if you happen across him in a dark alley, and says, “you his legal counsel?”

“I am indeed,” you say, clutching your legal pad like a shield. “The name’s Victoria Justice. Justice by name, Justice for all my clients.” You used to use this name during your brief career as a lawyer and always thought it had a nice ring.

Sherlock frowns. “Victoria Justice? Hey, isn’t that the name of an actress? Yeah, I’m sure it is-“

“I need to see my client,” you say quickly, aware that you should probably have checked to make sure there wasn't an actual person called Victoria Justice before picking the name. ”Now.”

“Yeah, yeah,” he mutters. “Hey, Evan, your lawyer’s here. Name of Victoria Justice.”

Evan looks at you but, due to your remarkable disguise, doesn't seem to recognise you. “Aren't you an actress?”

Sherlock, clearly not interested in listening in to your conversation with Evan, goes back to his magazine so you should be able to talk freely. You can ask him about his arrest, if he has an alibi, what evidence they have against him or anything else you like.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 207.

> Examine magazine
It’s one of those magazines. You know the sort. Where clothes are kinda missing the point and everyone is a fan of bananas and whipped cream. During your brief - very brief, believe me! - career as a professional model - you were young, okay? You needed the money - you came across this quite often. You’ve never been able to enjoy bananas or whipped cream since.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 209.

> Ask Evan about evidence
“The guy in charge - Whiteman, I think his name is-“

“Pinkerton.”

“Yeah, that’s him. They said they had an eyewitness who saw me creeping into Lord Montrose’s room with a knife and then creeping back out after he was dead. But it wasn’t me, miss! Honest it wasn’t.”

You need to get a look at Pinkerton’s files to see who this mystery eyewitness is. Could it be the real killer trying to frame someone else for the crime?

Pinkerton, flanked by several cronies who look quite a bit more disreputable than the people they're meant to be arresting, strides into the ballroom and says, "ladies and gentlemen, I'm pleased to announce that the investigation is over. The killer has been caught."

There's a round of applause in the ballroom. Someone says, "well done, that man!" while someone else says, "thank heavens for that!" and someone else says (because someone else always says it), "this calls for a drink!"

"We have someone in custody right now," says Pinkerton, "and I'm quietly confident that he will soon confess-"

"Evan is no killer," says Joves and every eye turns to him. "The real killer is still out there. Do not close the investigation, officer. You still have work to do."

"We have our man," says Pinkerton. "Rest assured on that."

Joves rolls his eyes and heads back to his office.

"As I was saying before I was rudely interrupted," Pinkerton says, casting an angry look at Joves' retreating back, "the investigation is over and we have our man. And now I'm heading off to the sitting room to relax. If anyone has any questions, or if they wish to obtain my autograph, I'll be free for several hours yet."

Pinkerton and his cronies depart, followed by several of the nobility who no doubt wish for his fleeting fame to rub off on them.

"You see, darling?" says Lord Whatever. "Everything worked out for the best."

You aren't so sure about that yourself. This day just goes from bad to worse.

________________________________The main area of the guest house has been converted into a base of operations for the police, who are apparently hard at work. You walk into the middle of a battlefield (or so it seems)! Two cops - of the hulking one-brain-cell-between-the-pair-of-them variety - are squaring up to each other, fists raised and tempers flared while several other cops are gathered around looking like this is the best thing they've witnessed all day. This brings back memories of your time - very briefly - as a bare knuckle brawler when people would gather around and place bets on how many times you'd kick your opponent in the groin and get away with it.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 212.

Just when it looks like things might get interesting (for interesting, read bloody), Bribeasy steps between them and demands, "what the devil is going on, fellows?" he demands.

"Rockford's said my wife is ugly," one of the brawlers says. "So I'm gonna teach him a lesson he ain't gonna forget."

"She is ugly, she's got a face like a walrus" says Rockford. This sentiment is echoed by several of the other officers.

"Why you little-"

"The pair of you," says Bribeasy. "Come with me. Now!"

Looking like a couple of children caught misbehaving, the two cops follow Bribeasy outside.

Pinkerton's Office
EXITS: NORTHWEST

SCORE 212/283; TURNS TAKEN 950

________________________________Much of the clutter from before has been cleared away with just the desk Pinkerton was using and a stack of files remaining. Now that Evan has been arrested, Pinkerton probably thinks the whole thing is over and done with.

> Examine files
A familiar name jumps out at you the moment you look at the first file: Silas! It seems he provided a report to Pinkerton that he had seen Evan sneaking into Lord Montrose's room right before the murder and Pinkerton, fifth rate excuse for a cop that he is, believed him hook, line and sinker. If you know Pinkerton and his fondness for simply arresting the first suspect and trying to convict him because it’s easier than finding the actual guilty party, he’ll simply bury Evan under a mountain of circumstantial evidence and not look any further. After all, it doesn’t matter to him whether the right person is arrested, just that someone is. Pinkerton just needs to arrest anyone who doesn’t have an alibi and make sure they go down. This is bad…

Or is it? Is it really a problem? Think about it. What does it matter to you if Lord Montrose’s killer escapes justice? You don’t owe him a thing. And why should you care if Evan gets convicted of a crime he didn’t commit? He’s just a lovesick fool. You could walk away from this, let the killer escape justice, let Evan rot in a cell for the rest of his life and marry Lord Whatever and be rich. Filthy stinking rich. You’re not one of those morons who try to do the right thing just because it’s the right thing. You’re in this for number one.

Stay or flee that’s the choice you have right now.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 213.

> Stay
Well, would you look at that? You do have a conscience after all. Given the choice between leaving some poor schmuck to his fate and living the high life, you actually decided to stay and do the decent thing. Good for you.

“Shut up, you idiot,” you mutter and your conscience, thankfully, does just that.

Now you need to provide Pinkerton with proof that Evan has been set up. Lazy and incompetent though Pinkerton is, you grudgingly admit that he’s only actually borderline corrupt. If you can provide him with proof that Evan has been framed, he'll reopen the investigation. The question is… how?

“But, sir-“

Pinkerton disappears into his office and Bribeasy storms away, muttering that he needs a drink.

Interesting. So at least one cop is more interested in doing the job properly instead of simply blindly following around. You need to have a word with Bribeasy.

Den
EXITS: NORTHWEST

SCORE 223/283; TURNS TAKEN 995
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________A lavish bar occupies one whole wall and looks to contain every beer known to man, and likely a few others as well. In the main area of the den is a large sofa set before a roaring oak fire and in the corner is a bed. It might be just your imagination, but you get the distinct impression that this isn't the kind of bed that sees much sleeping. It's the kind of bed used for... other activities. Bribeasy is sitting on the sofa.

> Talk to Bribeasy
Bribeasy listens uneasily to what you tell him. “This isn’t good,” he says when you’ve finished. “This Old Man Micawber sounds like a right piece of work, but at least from what you told me Pinkerton might not think Evan is the killer, so maybe some good has come of it. Saying that, knowing what Pinkerton’s like for always wanting a conviction no matter the cost, he might still try and pin it all on Evan anyway. We need someone to provide an alibi for Evan at the time he was supposedly killing Lord Montrose. Do that and we can hopefully stop Pinkerton framing Evan for the murder. Think. Have you talked to anyone who mentioned Evan? If you have, whisper me their name so I can go have a chat to them myself."

Know the name in question? Good for you. Say it to Bribeasy in the format 'whisper [name]' and see how it goes.

> Whisper Carmichael
"Carmichael? The two foot windbag? He was questioned earlier but never made mention of Evan. Then again, I think he spent the whole time bragging about some fictional journey he supposedly went on, so anything useful he knew was probably forgotten. Right, I'm going to have a word with him."

Bribeasy strides confidently away.
