Pokey Passage
EXITS: WEST, DOWN

SCORE 225/283; TURNS TAKEN 1005
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________You're at the end of a somewhat pokey passage next to an open door. Seriously, this place has sinister shadows like they were going out of fashion and seems completely out of place in the mansion, almost as if you've stepped into a Hammer Horror remake. Set into the wall by the door is a battered bell and even that looks creepier than any bell has a right to look.  Carmichael is here, looking nervous.

“Carmichael!” Bribeasy calls as he walks into the pokey passage, causing Carmichael to give a nervous start. “We need to talk.”

Immediately, several passersby swivel to pay attention in case Bribeasy is going to arrest Carmichael or perhaps just beat him to a pulp.

Carmichael flinches as if expects the latter. “Now steady on, there’s a good chap. I’m sure we can come to some sort of-“

“Evan. Were you with him when Lord Montrose was murdered?”

“Er, yes, I believe I was-“

“Why didn’t you say anything when you were questioned earlier?”

“I, uh, well…” Carmichael looks nervously around. “Does it matter?”

“Does it- Come on, you pompous ass! You’re coming with me.”

“Where to?”

“To see my boss,” Bribeasy says as he frog-marches Carmichael from the passage.

Several eyes turn away, disappointed. “He could at least have shot the fellow,” someone is heard to remark.

“Carmichael!” Bribeasy calls as he walks into the pokey passage, causing Carmichael to give a nervous start. “We need to talk.”

Immediately, several passersby swivel to pay attention in case Bribeasy is going to arrest Carmichael or perhaps just beat him to a pulp.

Carmichael flinches as if expects the latter. “Now steady on, there’s a good chap. I’m sure we can come to some sort of-“

“Evan, were you with him when Lord Montrose was murdered?”

“Er, yes, I believe I was-“

“Why didn’t you say anything when you were questioned earlier?”

“I, uh, well…” Carmichael looks nervously around. “Does it matter?”

“Does it- Come on, you pompous. You’re coming with me.”

“Where to?”

“To see my boss,” Bribeasy says as he frog-marches Carmichael from the passage.

Several eyes turn away, disappointed. “He could at least have shot the fellow,” someone is heard to remark.

Lobby
EXITS: SOUTH, EAST, NORTHWEST, UP

SCORE 225/283; TURNS TAKEN 1006
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________The lobby of Montrose Mansion is not quite as chaotic as when you first arrived, due to the absence of the assembled clucking nobility who have been moved on by the police. A route is now visible to the south, which leads outside to the gardens, and there is a previously hidden corridor to the east. And there's a rather large statue of Lord Montrose overlooking the lobby, which you're sure must have been visible before but you don't remember seeing any sign of it. The overly large ego of some noble no doubt hid it from view. Oh, and there are some banners advertising the appeals of the art gallery hanging from the stairs. Very well done, too, though you say so yourself.  Carmichael is here, looking nervous.

“Boss!” Bribeasy calls as he strides into the lobby. “Got someone here who needs a word.”

Pinkerton, on his way into the mansion, has a put-upon look on his face. “Again, Bribeasy? What is it this time?”

Bribeasy glares at Carmichael, who promptly faints.

“Bravo, fellow,” says Pinkerton, giving a mocking clap. “You've excelled yourself again. I do hope he's dead as we've already got enough dead nobles around here for one day.”

In due course, however, Carmichael is revived (Bribeasy kicking him up the backside and muttering “wake up, you useless waste of space!” probably doesn't help but it’s something that was definitely worth the effort in your opinion) and relates his story of talking with Evan when Joves announced that Lord Montrose had been murdered, which means that Evan couldn't have killed anyone.

“This could all be an elaborate scheme the two cooked up between them to commit the murder,” says Pinkerton, clutching at straws with the fervour of someone who really thought he was going to get a promotion and now that promotion is slipping swiftly away.

“Do you think either of them have got the wits to cook up anything?” Bribeasy asks. "Evan is borderline dim-witted and this guy... well, it's not very borderline at all."

Pinkerton deflates with a depressed sigh. He knows when he's beaten. “Good point. They're both so stupid I should probably have them arrested for it.”

“Hey, I’m stood right here,” Carmichael protests, and is promptly ignored.

“I’ll release Evan for now,” says Pinkerton. “And reopen the investigation. And I’ll be having a serious word with the fellow who gave me the witness report of Evan creeping out of Lord Montrose’s bedroom with a knife.”

And with that, Pinkerton heads back to the guest house, Bribeasy goes to see to Evan’s release, and Carmichael, still being ignored, goes off in a huff.

Your score has increased by 3 points to 228.

Cells

________________________________Who knew there were cells at Montrose Mansion? Bribeasy enters the cells and Sherlock immediately looks uneasy as if he instinctively knows that he'll be forced to do some work. "Release this man, Sherlock. He's innocent."

Evan looks faint with relief while Sherlock sighs. "Do we have to? I mean, the paperwork..."

"Did you complete the paperwork when he was booked in?"

Sherlock looks relieved. "Musta slipped my mind what with all my other duties." He goes over to the occupied cell and unlocks it. "Alright, son, you're free to go. Don't find yourself back here, okay?"

Evan staggers from the cell. "Oh, this is such a relief. Sophia! I have to go and see her. She'll be ever so worried about me."

As he leaves, Bribeasy glances at you. "I'll be returning to my duties in the guest house. Evan's free, thank god, but we've still got a killer to apprehend."

Leaving just you and Sherlock, and his magazine. Yes, it's already made a reappearance.

Perkins' Room
EXITS: SOUTHWEST

SCORE 228/283; TURNS TAKEN 1016
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Very few rooms in the mansion could ever be considered ‘charming’ or ‘homely’ and this one is no exception. What it lacks in charming and homely, however, it more than makes up for with a chilling draft and a window which could be deemed as both open and closed at the same time. Other than this, there’s the bed - at least you assume it’s a bed but you’re willing to admit you could be wrong - and something that might be a beer cooler, if it wasn't placed right next to an open log fire.

Technically you guess this is now Satan's room and not Perkins' room but whoever handles the updates for this of thing is clearly slacking. The man in question is stood nearby, looking not very impressed with his new accommodation.

> Ask Satan about Joves
"We have a very complicated relationship: he quietly detests me while I openly detest him. Nothing will change until he comes to his senses and apologises for his part in my mother leaving."

> Ask Satan about mother
"She was an alcoholic and a cheat and a thief and a murderer - all of which I put solely at his feet. When the police questioned my father about the man my mother was alleged to have killed, did he move heaven and earth to try and save her? He did not! He as good as abandoned her when the only evidence against her was DNA evidence, fingerprints, eyewitnesses, security cameras and a signed confession. He would not even give her the benefit of the doubt when the murder weapon was found under her bed! That is why I will never forgive him. Ask him about it if you like. It does me good to open old wounds. Ask him about his dear Froghilda and see what he says."

> SW

Joves' Office
EXITS: SOUTHEAST

SCORE 228/283; TURNS TAKEN 1021
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________You can't help but think that the office of the butler is very much like the man himself: cold, lifeless and utterly lacking in personality. Sure, it has the usual suspects - desk, drinks cabinet, files, boring painting on the wall next to an ancient bell - but done in such a way as if to suggest 'this is dull. Move along. Nothing to see here.' Joves is sat at his desk.

"So Evan's free, is he?" says Joves. "Good. When you see him next, make sure he knows I'm docking his pay for the time he was locked up." At your bemused expression, he adds, "I'm not running a charity here."

> Ask Joves about Froghilda
"Ah, my darling wife," says Joves with more than a hint of bitterness. "I'm guessing you've been talking to Satan. He's never forgiven me for my part in her troubles."

> Ask Joves about troubles
"She had problems. No, she was the problem! Drugs, drink, smoking, she even tried her hand at line dancing one time." He shudders. "Worrying behaviour, and dangerous besides when you have an impressionable young man living there. I wondered what kind of man Satan would grow up to become if she was there. But fate intervened before I could act. She was arrested for killing someone."

> Ask Joves about killing
"Some reprehensible lowlife she had met. I think they used to rob casinos and banks together. One time, they apparently had a disagreement over the splitting of the loot from one of their many robberies: he wanted a 50/50 division whereas she wanted it all. They fought. He died of a gunshot. Eyewitnesses placed her at the scene and with her previous history of offending, it didn't take the police long to track her down. And the rest, as they say, is history. She was arrested and given a life sentence and Satan, only a boy at the time, held me responsible for not trying to defend her. He's never forgiven me. One day, I'd like to make peace with him but he's nothing if not stubborn."

> Ask Joves about peace
"I have no idea how I'd even go about it. Satan might be my son but we're strangers most of the time. I got him the job here years ago but he's barely even spoken to me since then. Is there anything you can think of that I might do to repair this rift between us? Maybe you could speak to him on my behalf and ask him about a possible reconciliation."

> SE

> Ask Joves about Emma
“Interesting,” he says after a moment. “He is prepared to consider a reconciliation.”

“But he wants Emma back,” you say. “Didn’t she leave?”

Joves nods. “She did, but I wonder… The police have the mansion under lockdown and no one is allowed to leave so unless she has somehow snuck past them, she is still here somewhere. We simply need to find her. Tell me, have you encountered anyone among the police who might know more? If so, go to them and ask them about Emma. With luck, we can get her back with my son and hopefully salvage something from this unfortunate day.”

"Anything to report, men?" Pinkerton asks as he strides back into the guest house. "We caught any murderers lately?"

His question is met with muted responses ranging from "nah" to "what murder?" to "what's on TV?"

Pinkerton sighs. "I'll be in my room. Oswald, come talk to me."

He heads into the room he's taken over and one of the cops follows him.

> Ask Bribeasy about Emma
Bribeasy frowns. "Emma? Yes, that name sounds familiar. I believe someone call Emma was stopped trying to leave by the main gate earlier and she didn't seem very pleased to be told that no one could leave until the investigation was over. I'm not sure where she is now but she ran off into the gardens so I'd probably start there."

Pinkerton's Office
EXITS: NORTHWEST

SCORE 228/283; TURNS TAKEN 1048
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Formerly the office of the guest house manager, now the office of none other than your nemesis, Pinkerton, who is, at this precise moment, sat at the desk fast asleep. There are a number of files on the desk, fighting for room with beer bottles and several pizza boxes, while in the corner he's placed a crate marked 'evidence' (and a few more beer bottles). Considering how little time has passed since the murder, you're quite impressed at how quickly Pinkerton has made this place a total dump. Credit where credit is due, the man is a pillock of the first order.

Pinkerton looks up as you enter, looks about to ask what you're doing, then shrugs as if it's not worth pursuing any further.

"Oswald, I've got a bit of a quandary here," he says to the officer stood by his desk. "You remember how I told you my old man works here and he's no stranger to the criminal world?"

"No, sir. I don't think you've ever spoken to me before today, sir."

Pinkerton frowns. "Well, anyway. He is no stranger to the criminal world and it's a big problem for someone in my profession. Every time I know of some big criminal enterprise going down, I have to wonder if he's involved and, if so, how I handle it. Do I arrest my own dad? Do I turn a blind eye? I wonder how my superiors will act and I doubt it'll go well for me however I act. I'm in a bit of a predicament, Oswald. What do you think?"

"Um… sorry, sir, but… I kinda got lost for a second there…"

Pinkerton sighs. "Dismissed, man. Go back to your job and do whatever it is you do all day."

Oswald scarpers.

Pinkerton then turns to you and frowns. "And what are you doing in here? Say, you look ever so familiar-"

You scarper, too.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 229.

Stables
EXITS: NORTHEAST

SCORE 229/283; TURNS TAKEN 1057
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________As with most of the buildings on the Montrose grounds, the stables are remarkably rundown: most of the walls sag to one side, the floor audibly creaks underfoot and even the air has a neglected feel to it. The fact that only a single horse - a single ancient horse - is stabled here doesn't help either. As such, it's perhaps hardly surprising that there's a single hostler, called (of all things) Sally Dobbin, managing things, and as she's staring into space... well, it says it all really.  You see Emma, one of the serving girls, here.

You see Emma pacing back and forth in the stables, clearly furious.

"That impossible man gets me fired and now I can't even leave the mansion," she says to Sally. "How long am I supposed to stay here? Murder investigations can take years! I can't wait here for years! I might run into... him…"

"Just lay low for a while," says Sally. "I'm sure the cops will let everyone leave before too much longer. And Satan won't come here. After our little fling, he's avoided me like the plague."

"He got me fired! And he thought it was what I wanted-" She pauses, noticing you there for the first time. "Oh, please don't tell me you're here at Satan's behest. I'm more likely to murder that man right now than give him another chance. Go tell him that if you like."

> Talk to Emma
You explain that you came here at Joves' behest - "he's just as bad," Emma says with a scowl - and not Satan's - "that guy needs a smack," - and that you're hoping Emma will come back to work at the mansion - "fat chance!" - and give Satan a second chance - a very unladylike snort!

"Not likely," she says without even thinking it through. "I'm done with this place. As soon as the cops let me leave, I'm out of here. I might head for the coast and try my hand at singing in a bar. It's what I've always wanted to do. Say, Satan wants to make amends? Tell him it'll help if he can get my old gramophone fixed. It's been gathering dust in the storage room for months now because I couldn't afford to pay for the repairs and he always refused. He fixes it now, maybe - and that's a small maybe - I'll think about giving him another chance." She shrugs. "Or maybe I'll just sell it for cash and laugh at Satan for thinking I'd give him another chance."

> NE

________________________________A storage room of junk by the look of things, and not the kind of junk that anyone thinks might be useless but more a case of 'just chuck it in here and forget about it' kind of junk. Do you need a broken piano, a pool table (minus any balls or cues) or a guillotine (minus its blade)? No? Well, too bad. Other than that there are the well-placed sacks you landed on when you descended from above, a sturdy door in the west wall and an open panel in the ceiling and that's your lot. Anything useful? Well…

Something's changed. You can tell that from a glance. The gramophone is missing! And someone has left muddy footprints where it used to be!

> Examine muddy footprints
Very muddy indeed. If you had to guess, you'd say whoever took the gramophone had recently been in the gardens.

You don't even see much food being cooked. There's a large pile of it on a counter but it's still uncooked and no one seems to be in much of a hurry to change that situation.

Abrams' Hut
EXITS: NORTH

SCORE 229/283; TURNS TAKEN 1086
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________There's not a whole lot you can think to say about this hut, but the words 'ramshackle', 'rundown' and 'craphole' spring to mind. It had a roof, once. Now? It just has the absence of a roof. You're sure it also once had furniture, now it just has a burnt bed, a burnt chair and, you guessed it, a burnt table. One wall is given over to a woodwork display which could charitably be described as 'a bit naff'. And the hole where the roof used to be. Yep, that's a real eyesore.  Abrams the gardener is here, having a good scratch.

> Ask Abrams about gramophone
"Gramo-wotsit? Nah, lass, I ain't been seein' no gramo-wotsit 'round 'ere," says Abrams with the kind of shadiness you've come to expect from people who are lying through their teeth. "I, er, dunno anythin' 'bout gramo-wotsits."

Interesting. You'll have to keep an eye on him. Maybe if you wait a while, you can trick him into giving something away.

> Wait
Abrams looks at you impatiently. "Ain't you got anywhere else to be, lass?"

"No," you say. "I'm fine right where I am."

He scowls.

> Wait
"Did you 'ear that?" asks Abrams. "Sounded jus' like someone callin' your name."

"I didn't hear anything," you say. "But I'm sure if it's important, they'll call again."

He scowls some more.

> Wait
"Bah!" Abrams curses. "Fine! I tooks the darn gramophone, you evil harlot! I was gonna play some classic tunes to wins over Sally - but it don't even works! It be broken. So I gives it to that Tarquin fellow 'cos he said he knew someone what could fix it. 'Appy?"

Your score has increased by 1 point to 230.

Library
EXITS: NORTHEAST

SCORE 230/283; TURNS TAKEN 1098
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Ah, the library of Montrose Mansion. You've heard of this place but the reality certainly fails to live up to its reputation. Where are the rows and rows of books covering every subject under the sun? Instead you see shelves which are mostly empty, books which look to have been thrown haphazardly around - some missing covers or spines or, in a few cases, everything in between as well - and a very bored looking librarian currently playing cards and yawning profusely. You don't even see any of the famed reading chairs purchased at great expense from abroad and shipped here at great personal expense. Instead, there's just a hard wooden bench on which the librarian is playing cards (meaning you don't even have a place to sit). Actually, you do see one chair, tucked away in the corner, but that's occupied by Bombur, no doubt still fuming from his argument with Scrimmage.  Tarquin is here, perusing some books.

> Ask Tarquin about gramophone
"Yeah, I got a gramophone but the damn thing's broke," he says with a scowl. “And when I told Abrams I could fix it, well… that was a bit of a lie. I do know someone who is good at fixing things,” he adds quickly as if you were about to doubt him, “but he’s, er, not available right now.”

“He’s in prison, you mean,” you hazard a guess.

“Yes, and this fixing lark isn’t half as straightforward as I’d thought it’d be. I figured I’d just screw a few things down, tap it a few times, curse at it and it’d be fixed. But no. Now I got a broken gramophone on my hands I can’t mend and Abrams asking me when it’s going to be fixed and dropping hints that he won’t wait forever.”

“I could take it off your hands for you,” you offer.

Tarquin gives you a suspicious look. “You do that and Abrams will be coming after you for fixing it.”

“Leave me to deal with Abrams.”

He still looks suspicious, as if he suspects you’ll just swipe the gramophone for yourself and leave him high and dry (which, funnily enough, is exactly what you intend to do), but figure it must be worth it because he says he’s got the gramophone hidden in the den in the gardens.

“I’ve been to the den,” you say. “I don’t remember seeing any gramophone there.”

“Ah, but I hid it real well…” And he tells you just how to find it.

> NE

EXITS: NORTHWEST

________________________________A lavish bar occupies one whole wall and looks to contain every beer known to man, and likely a few others as well. You head over to the spot Tarquin told you to look and, sure enough, there’s a broken old gramophone hidden there.

Broken? That’s the understatement of the year. It’s so battered and decrepit that if it was in ten times the condition it’s in right now, it would still be too useless to count as broken. There’s no way Emma will accept this. As little as you want to, you don't seem to have any other choice than to take it back to Abrams and ask if there’s anyone else he might know that would be able to fix it. It’s certainly nothing you could do yourself.

> Ask Abrams about gramophone
“Yeah,” he says sadly, “it ain’t well, is it?”

“Do you know anyone else who might be able to fix it?”

“Well, there’s one guy but…” He scowls. “I didn’t wan’ to go to ‘im ‘cos he’s the sort o’ fellow who always wants somethin’ for ‘is ‘elp. Fellow can’t jus’ ‘elp you out ‘cos it’s the decent thing to do.”

"Well, fancy that," you mutter.

Abrams, however, seems oblivious to your sarcasm. "It be Micawber. You'll find 'im nearby. Ask 'im 'bout fixin' the gramophone an' see what he says."

The gardens of Montrose Mansion are very pretty but, at the same time, very dull. Seriously, how many times can you look at a flower or bush before you succumb to the desire to claw your eyes out? You're currently in a part of the gardens which looks exactly the same as all the other parts. Sometimes, nature just doesn't even make an effort. Sitting here on a decrepit bench is Old Man Micawber, who you understand is the odd jobs man at the mansion. Curled up under the bench is his cat, Yerviciousbastard, reputedly the most bad-tempered cat in the known world.

> Ask Micawber about gramophone
"Want it fixin' do you? Well, I can see to that rightly so but…"

"You want something in return?" you hazard a guess.

"Got it in one, lass. Me an' Joves, right, we 'ad a game at one time where we'd ask each other riddles. First one what couldn't answer the other's riddle lost. It were a game o' 'onour but… well, Joves musta cheated 'cos he kept winnin'. Every single time. I reckons he's got a riddle book in his room or his office, or 'idden on his person probably. Get me that book an' we'll see 'ow well he does wi'out it. That'll be our deal: that cheater's riddle book for my fixin' o' the gramophone."

> NE

Very well done, too, though you say so yourself.

Ballroom
EXITS: NORTH, SOUTH, EAST, NORTHWEST

Dining Room
EXITS: NORTH, EAST, WEST

SCORE 231/283; TURNS TAKEN 1127
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14

A feast that is, alas, going to waste right now as news of the murder has somewhat dampened people's appetites. Someone with more money than taste has hung several pieces of art on the far wall, none of it being to your fancy, framing a gothic archway while to the north is a large oak door.  A serving girl called Kristina is stood by the table, looking bored and not doing a very good job of hiding it.

Kitchen
EXITS: SOUTH, EAST, NORTHEAST, NORTHWEST

SCORE 231/283; TURNS TAKEN 1128
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________You might have expected the kitchen to be a hectic affair with a chef shouting orders, frantic workers running back and forth and a dozen meals being prepared at any given time, especially considering the size of the mansion and the sheer number of people here, but instead you find a fairly small room, very quiet, with the chef sitting on a stool reading a book, a cat drinking spilt milk off a table and nothing much in the way of cooking going on. You don't even see much food being cooked. There's a large pile of it on a counter but it's still uncooked and no one seems to be in much of a hurry to change that situation.

> NW

Joves' Office
EXITS: SOUTHEAST

SCORE 231/283; TURNS TAKEN 1129
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________You can't help but think that the office of the butler is very much like the man himself: cold, lifeless and utterly lacking in personality. Sure, it has the usual suspects - desk, drinks cabinet, files, boring painting on the wall next to an ancient bell - but done in such a way as if to suggest 'this is dull. Move along. Nothing to see here.' Joves is sat at his desk.

> Ask Joves about riddle book
"He wants what?" Joves scoffs. "I don't have a riddle book! I won because I'm far cleverer than he is, it's as simple as that. However, if it gets him to help with the fixing of the gramophone, give him this and tell him it's really my riddle book." He hands you a book titled Joves' Riddle Book. "What? It's the name that was written on the cover when I found it one day. It's just pure coincidence I assure you. But if it convinces that fool to help, then he can think what he likes.”

He hands over the riddle book.

Gardens
EXITS: NORTHEAST, NORTHWEST

SCORE 232/283; TURNS TAKEN 1140
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________
The gardens of Montrose Mansion are very pretty but, at the same time, very dull. Seriously, how many times can you look at a flower or bush before you succumb to the desire to claw your eyes out? You're currently in a part of the gardens which looks exactly the same as all the other parts. Sometimes, nature just doesn't even make an effort. Sitting here on a decrepit bench is Old Man Micawber, who you understand is the odd jobs man at the mansion. Curled up under the bench is his cat, Yerviciousbastard, reputedly the most bad-tempered cat in the known world.

> Give riddle book to Micawber
Old Man Micawber chortles as you hand him the book. “Oh, this be good, lass. Good indeed. Next time we ‘ave one o’ our riddles, we’ll see ‘ow well he does wi’out his precious book.” He chortles some more then looks at you. “Still ‘ere?”

“Gramophone,” you say pointedly.

“Ah, right. Well, it just so ‘appens that I got a gramophone right ‘ere.” And a brand new gramophone appears, as if by magic. Or at least some very questionable slight of hand.

You stare at it suspiciously. “You just had that here all along?”

Old Man Micawber nods. “Looks like it, lass. What are the odds, eh?”

“About a million to one,” you mutter. “I suppose if I happened to need a full scale model of the Titanic, you’d probably have one to hand, wouldn’t you?”

“Does you need a full scale model o’ the Titanic, lass?”

“No, no, just thinking out loud.”

You take the brand new gramophone and leave the old one with Old Man Micawber who will, no doubt, find a use for it somehow.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 233.

Stables
EXITS: NORTHEAST

SCORE 233/283; TURNS TAKEN 1145
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________As with most of the buildings on the Montrose grounds, the stables are remarkably rundown: most of the walls sag to one side, the floor audibly creaks underfoot and even the air has a neglected feel to it. The fact that only a single horse - a single ancient horse - is stabled here doesn't help either. As such, it's perhaps hardly surprising that there's a single hostler, called (of all things) Sally Dobbin, managing things, and as she's staring into space... well, it says it all really.  You see Emma, one of the serving girls, here.

> Give gramophone to Emma
Emma looks amazed, as if she never expected you to return with her fixed gramophone.

"I'm amazed," she says. "I never expected you to return with my fixed gramophone. I just figured you'd disappear and that'd be it."

"It looks quite nifty," says Sally. "I know someone who could sell this for a tidy sum."

Emma sighs. "I suppose I'd better go and talk to Satan then. Which I'm not looking forward to, but a deal's a deal. We'll see if he's changed."

Lugging her gramophone, she leaves the stables.

"Or," says Sally with a sigh, "you could just totally ignore me like I'm not even here."

Your score has increased by 1 point to 234.

Servants' Quarters (west)
EXITS: EAST, WEST, NORTHEAST

SCORE 234/283; TURNS TAKEN 1158

________________________________The rest of the mansion has a kind of “old money” charm to it, albeit rundown and shabby, but the servants' quarters are all very modern and thoroughly lacking in personality. And colour. In fact, the only colour in use here is gray, though it does come in many different shades (sadly all equally bland and unappealing). None of the servants you see seem willing to stop and chat, or even question why you, clearly not a servant, are in their quarters.

Perkins' Room
EXITS: SOUTHWEST

SCORE 234/283; TURNS TAKEN 1159
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Very few rooms in the mansion could ever be considered ‘charming’ or ‘homely’ and this one is no exception. What it lacks in charming and homely, however, it more than makes up for with a chilling draft and a window which could be deemed as both open and closed at the same time. Other than this, there’s the bed - at least you assume it’s a bed but you’re willing to admit you could be wrong - and something that might be a beer cooler, if it wasn't placed right next to an open log fire.

Technically you guess this is now Satan's room and not Perkins' room but whoever handles the updates for this of thing is clearly slacking. The man in question is stood nearby, looking not very impressed with his new accommodation.  You see Emma, one of the serving girls, here.

"Satan," Emma says and Satan looks up at her with a… well, not quite a smile but he comes close. It's the effort that counts, you guess. "I heard you got my gramophone fixed. Thank you."

"It was nothing," says Satan. He seems most un-Satan like for a moment. Almost… human. "A mere, um, trifle."

"You're not forgiven, buster. You got me fired and you didn't even care. But… well, you got my gramophone fixed and that’s hardly nothing so I’m willing to give you a second chance.” Emma sighs. “Now as soon as the cops let us leave, I need to find myself a new job.”

“No, you don’t,” Satan says. “Come with me.”

“Where to?”

Satan grimaces. “To see my father.”

Like a man about to face a terrible evil, Satan leaves the room, Emma following behind.

> SW

Joves' Office
EXITS: SOUTHEAST

SCORE 234/283; TURNS TAKEN 1162
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________You can't help but think that the office of the butler is very much like the man himself: cold, lifeless and utterly lacking in personality. Sure, it has the usual suspects - desk, drinks cabinet, files, boring painting on the wall next to an ancient bell - but done in such a way as if to suggest 'this is dull. Move along. Nothing to see here.' Joves is sat at his desk.

Joves looks up as Satan and Emma enter the room. A cold chill descends on the room. Emma immediately steps out of the way, perhaps fearing fists are about to start flying.

“What are you doing here?” they both say at the same time.

“I made you fire Emma,” says Satan. “That was wrong of me. I want you to reinstate her with full pay and an exemption from toilet cleaning duties.”

“I didn’t even know this place had toilets,” you mutter, wondering where on earth they are and thinking it's probably just as well that you have an unusually strong bladder.

“They’re very well hidden,” Emma says. “And believe me, that’s a good thing. Most of the nobility think that flushing the toilet is something that happens to other people.”

“Done,” says Joves. “I did think it was odd when Emma’s name showed up on that employee dismissal form but I figured it was just something I misremembered. However, for the time of her dismissal when she was not working, I will be docking her pay.”

Satan nods. “That’s perfectly understandable.”

“Hey!” says Emma. “I’m not having-“

Satan turns to her and hisses, “my dear, take the win.”

Emma fumes but realises that her best bet is just to keep quiet. “Very well, dear. I accept.”

“Good,” says Joves. “Emma, return to your duties forthwith. Satan, a word?”

Still fuming a little, Emma heads to the sitting room to resume her duties.

"It's time we buried the hatchet, son," Joves says. "For better or worse, we're family and we need to look out for one another at a time like this."

Satan sighs. "I guess you're right. I've always blamed you for what happened to mother, but I'm willing to admit that her being a hardened criminal with no scruples may have had more to do with her eventual incarceration than anything you did."

"Ah, son, it does me good to hear you say that." The two men hug with the awkwardness of two men who have likely never hugged anyone in their lives. "Aside from anything else, we might well be out of a job soon anyway."

“You don’t think Lady Montrose will keep us on then?”

Joves shakes his head sadly. “I doubt it. She’s never cared for either of us and, between you and me, I wouldn’t be at all surprised if she had a hand in the murder. Remember what happened with Galina after all…”

"Ah yes. Galina. It's a good job no one heard you say that name. I'd hate to think what might happen if someone knew of our suspicions regarding what happened to poor Galina."

After a brief moment, Satan returns to his room and Joves to his desk, apparently neither of them seeing you stood there the entire time.

Galina, eh?

Your score has increased by 3 points to 237.

> Ask Joves about Galina
“You overheard that? Well, it’s probably nothing but a few years ago, there was a young lady visiting the mansion that Lord Montrose had a thing for. His wife did not take it well. Hardly surprising, with him leaving his first wife after Sylvia came onto the scene. Anyway, after a blazing argument with his wife, Lord Montrose ordered the young lady, Galina was her name, to leave. That she ended up murdered immediately afterwards is, I’m quite sure, just an unfortunate coincidence.”

> Ask Joves about murdered
“Yes, her car broke down a few miles away and while she was waiting for a tow truck, someone ran her down.”

“What if it was just an accident?” you ask, thinking that accidents of this kind are very rarely accidents.

Joves shakes his head. “I doubt it. They also reversed over the corpse several times. By the time the ambulance arrived, they needed a shovel to cart her remains away instead of a stretcher. I’m not really sure why you’re asking me about Galina, though. She died several years ago. She can’t have anything to do with today’s events. Even if Sylvia had something to do with it..." He shakes his head. "No, I don't see it at all."

> Ask Lady Montrose about Galina
For a moment, the dim expression you’ve come to think of as ‘Lady Montrose to a tee’ slips and you get a quick view of what lies beneath. It’s not half as dim and a whole lot less friendly. Then in a moment it’s gone and she’s flashing you a dazzling smile. “That woman? Oh, please. I doubt she’s ever worn pink in her life.”

“I understand your husband had a thing for her.”

“Monty had a thing for every pretty thing that walked past him. I dare say, if you met him before today, you’d have probably been wiping slobber off your own dress. Have you not noticed how all the female servants are very pretty? Hardly by chance I can assure you. Anyway, Galina - the little harlot - is dead. Case closed. Now, if you'd be a dear and take a message to Kristina and tell her that I need to see her, I’d be ever so grateful.” She quickly writes a message out and hands it to you. “Don’t try reading it. It’s in my own shorthand.”

> Ask Joves about message
He looks at the message and frowns deeply. "This is worrying. Do you know what this message says?"

"No."

"It says that you may be onto something and you need to be dealt with. It says to contact 'him' - it doesn't say who that might be - and arrange for a little 'accident'." He tears the message up. "So, Sylvia is behind it after all, eh? Well, I'll be having words with her-"

"No," you say, a plan forming in your mind, "we'd just tip our hand and she'll deny everything. Write a second message, saying I've been recruited by Sylvia to help out and I need to see 'him' and we'll see what happens."

"I like it," says Joves. "Minimal risk to me and I get to share in the glory if you succeed." He writes a second message, and manages a very good imitation of Sylvia's handwriting. "Give that to Kristina and see what she does. I apologise in advance if she realises anything is wrong and has you killed, but it's hard to mimic someone's style with 100% accuracy."

He hands you the message and wishes you the best of luck.

Conference Room
EXITS: WEST

SCORE 239/283; TURNS TAKEN 1198
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________At least, you assume it's a conference room, or used to be anyway. These days it's just a big empty room with the wreckage of many old tables and chairs scattered around a central podium. And dust. Don't forget the dust. The east wall is given over to a large window, but one that doesn't let in much light due to the myriad of cracks which mar its surface.

> Wait
You wait… and wait… and wait…

And just as you’re getting tired of waiting and wondering if anything is going to happen, it does. But it’s definitely not anything good.

Silas steps into the conference room with a frown. “I couldn’t believe it when Kristina said Lady Montrose wanted me to meet you. After all the trouble you’ve caused, you’re the last person I expected to be working with.”

“I just wanted to know what was going on,” you say, “and how it affected my own plans."

"Plans?" Silas sneers. "We didn't kill Montrose because of a 'plan'. We killed him because of how corrupt he is and because of how he treats his staff.”

Interesting. So Silas, despite being, in your opinion, a wet-behind-the-ears idiot, is involved. But is it just him, Lady Montrose and Kristina or are other people involved? You need to find more about what is going on. “That doesn't ring true," you say. "Everyone I’ve spoken to says he was a great boss.”

“What would they know? Lady Montrose knows the truth and that’s what counts!" Spoken like a true madman. "Anyway, that doesn’t matter right now. Some fool helped clear the guy we framed for the murder so the police are still investigating around here and we need to get them moved on. You can help with that. I was originally going to frame Joves for the murder but Lady Montrose wasn’t sure anyone would buy it so we went with Evan, but now we’ll go back to Joves and to hell with whether anyone believes it. The first stage is to plant evidence in his room then have the police conveniently 'find' it. If you want to help, you plant this." He hands you a handkerchief. "One of Lord Montrose's, wet with his blood. Put it in Joves' room and I'll tip the police off."

Silas gives you a pointed look, as if he doesn't completely trust you, and hurries from the conference room.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 240.

Boat Shed
EXITS: NORTHEAST, DOWN

SCORE 241/283; TURNS TAKEN 1220
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________There's a flickering light bulb hanging from the dusty ceiling. Why is this relevant? Simply because the things you would normally expect to seer in a boat shed - top of the list being a boat and water - are strangely absent. Your attention is drawn to a ladder set into the floor, formerly hidden by a trapdoor (now thoroughly smashed to pieces thanks to yours truly).

The moment you step into the boat shed, you get an uneasy feeling. A feeling of wrongness. Even though you can’t see anyone, you get the distinct impression that you’re not alone. Someone very dangerous is here.

From the shadows, something moves... there’s a sharp intake of breath...

And a young girl, maybe ten years old, and small for her age, steps into view.

“Hiya,” she says with a bright smile, “I’m Whimsy. Me dad sent me. He said sorry he’s not here himself but me mum wanted him to do the shopping so he sent me instead. Hope that’s okay.”

Is this a joke? The nasty piece of work sent his ten year old daughter in his place?

“Lead the way, boss lady,” says Whimsy. “I’ll hang back here in the shadows if it’s okay with you ‘cos I’m kinda shy. Don’t worry though. I’ll still be here.”

Whimsy... doesn’t disappear but she becomes so much a part of the background that she might as well be invisible and if you didn’t know she was there, you’d never see her.

“Ready when you are, boss lady,” says a creepy voice out of nowhere. “Lead the way.”

You'd better go and meet Joves outside Lady Montrose's chambers and see what he says. Something tells you that he won't be best pleased.

> NE

Imposing Corridor
EXITS: NORTH, SOUTH

SCORE 241/283; TURNS TAKEN 1233
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Few corridors could properly be described as imposing, but then few corridors have screaming faces carved into the walls. Very imposing; also, a tad worrying. The door to the north, likewise imposing, is guarded by a man who probably doubles as a mountain in his spare time. Yes, he's that big. And imposing.

You could hear the argument before you reached the corridor: Joves ordering the giant guard to stand aside and the giant guard... well, not really arguing but simply standing there blocking the way in the manner that only people who are eight feet tall and build like an armoured tank carrier can.

“I order you to move out of the way this instant!” Joves says.

The giant guard says nothing.

“If you don’t move, I’ll have you fired,” says Joves.

The giant guard says nothing.

“This is your last chance so you’d better move or else!” says Joves.

The giant guard says nothing.

"I will call the police and have you arrested for interfering in a murder investigation!" says Joves.

The giant guard says nothing.

Joves sighs, defeated and turns to you. “He won’t listen to reason. Well, I guess that means we have no choice. Pibb, do your thing.”

“Um... Pibb couldn’t make it,” you say. “So, er, he sent his daughter.”

Whimsy steps out of the shadows. “Hi,” she says brightly. "Me dad says he's sorry but, well, me mum's a terror when she's in a bad mood and he don't want to get on her bad side. He's sure you'll understand."

Joves looks down at Whimsy. A long way down. If anything, she looks even smaller than she did back at the boat house as if she's suddenly shrunk between there and here. Joves closes his eyes, counts to ten, then opens them again. When the situation hasn’t resolved itself, and Whimsy hasn’t magically transformed into a brutish killing machine, he groans loudly.

“Only,” says Whimsy, who is clearly not good at reading the room, “me dad says I’m not allowed to do anything for you until you sign his last contract.”

“This is hardly the time, young lady!”

“Sorry, pal, but thems the rules. Me dad's a real stickler for them rules."

Joves says at you, "the contract wasn’t paid because Silas stole it out of my office - probably to cause trouble if I know him. You’ve been all over the mansion today. Is it too much hope that you’ve found the contract in question? I doubt Silas would simply destroy it because it could be used against me but I’ve no idea where he might hide it.”

"You're honouring the contract at a time like this?" you say, all too aware of the giant guard looming nearby. And there's a lot of him to loom.

"Believe me, I have enough problems without worrying about someone like Pibb Popsicle coming after me for breach of contract. Please, if you know where the contract is, fetch it for me. One problem dealt with at a time."

> Give contract to Whimsy
Whimsy studies the contract. “You going to pay this then ‘cos me dad won’t be happy if you welch on the debt.”

“It will be paid,” says Joves. “You have my word on that.”

“Okay.” She slips the contract into her pocket and steps up to the giant guard. “Move, pal. I’m not going to ask twice.”

The guard looks at her. Looks down at her. She's so small he could probably crush her by flexing his big toe. “Beat it, brat, before you get your teeth handed back to you.”

“Is she really going to fight him?” you ask Joves, a little concerned that you may just have sent a young girl to her death.

“I fear so,” says Joves solemnly. “That poor guard-“

There’s a howl from the guard followed by a scream of monstrous proportions. Everything happens so fast it’s hard to see what is going on but you think the giant guard may have a small girl’s teeth attached to his nose. He staggers back and forth, screaming loud enough to wake the dead, but the biting only becomes more intense. Blood splatters everywhere. Yelling in pain, the guard flees, the small girl still hanging from his face.

“We should leave them to it,” says Joves, shaking his head sadly. “We need to speak to Lady Montrose.”

He heads north into the room.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 243.

> N

Lady Montrose's Chambers
EXITS: SOUTH, NORTHWEST

SCORE 243/283; TURNS TAKEN 1235
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 27/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________Pink. These chambers are very pink. Incredibly pink. Exceedingly pink. Clearly, the owner of these chambers has a thing for the colour pink. There's the bed (pink), a bureau (also pink), a wardrobe (likewise pink), some fruit (they're probably meant to be oranges but, well, they're not) and a recliner (which, oddly enough, is blue). Lady Montrose has now departed but she's left behind a passage in the north wall. Joves is stood next to it, looking anxious.

After all the hassle of getting in here, you're disappointed to find that Lady Montrose is nowhere to be seen. Her chambers do, however, seem to have gained a secret passage in the north wall which is how you guess she's fled.

Joves pokes his head into the passage and then declares, "clearly, one of us needs to wait here in case she comes back this way while the other pursues her into the passage. Well, go on then," he adds with a glance into the passage.

You eye the passage nervously. While you can't see any, you'd bet your soul (assuming you have one, opinion on the subject is divided) that it's full of spiders and other creepy crawlies and you know from past experience during your tomb raider days (long story, don't ask) that they definitely disagree with you. "Are you sure it wouldn't make more sense for you to head into the passage while I stay behind in this chamber?"

"In this day and age?" says Joves. "Egads no! Why, I'd be in danger of being cancelled if I went ahead into the passage and left the woman here in safety."

Bugger. He's certainly got a point there.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 245.

Gardens
EXITS: NORTHEAST, NORTHWEST

SCORE 245/283; TURNS TAKEN 1248
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 28/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 9/14
________________________________
The gardens of Montrose Mansion are very pretty but, at the same time, very dull. Seriously, how many times can you look at a flower or bush before you succumb to the desire to claw your eyes out? You're currently in a part of the gardens which looks exactly the same as all the other parts. Sometimes, nature just doesn't even make an effort. Sitting here on a decrepit bench is Old Man Micawber, who you understand is the odd jobs man at the mansion. Curled up under the bench is his cat, Yerviciousbastard, reputedly the most bad-tempered cat in the known world.

> Ask Micawber about waterfall
"The waterfall, eh? By 'eck, it be years since I heard 'bout that. It used to be the big talkin' point 'round the mansion back when Brubaker were in charge and it were called Brubaker Mansion. You found one entrance I takes it, but 'as you found the other one?"

You wait. He waits. You sigh. He grins.

You say, "okay, what do you need from me to tell you where the other entrance is?"

"Nice o' you to ask, lass. I been 'ankerin' after some French cheese I has. Proper nice it is, too, much nicer 'n' the English stuff they get 'ere at the kitchen. But expensive, too. Horribly expensive. If you was to get me some, well, I mights jus' 'member where the other entrance to the waterfall is."

"And where would I find French cheese?"

"France," is the predictable answer, "but they can prob'ly get some in the kitchen if you asks nicely."

Now, hurry up and give him his ‘French cheese’ so we can find out how to get past the waterfall before Lady Montrose is out of reach.”

> Give French cheese to Micawber
Old Man Micawber takes the French cheese somewhat gingerly and stares it, perhaps wondering if French cheese is supposed to drip like this.

“Well, eat it then,” you say, quite hoping that he does. It’ll certainly be something worth seeing. During your time as a trainee nurse (footnote 5), you saw quite a few nauseating sights, but you doubt any of them would quite match a man eating cheese dripping with French aftershave.

“Maybe later,” he says, and then without even risking his life he puts the cheese to one side. “The other way inna the waterfall, well… you been into the greenhouse yet?  It be in there.”

“I never saw a way to the waterfall when I was there earlier.”

“Ah, but did ya dance?” Old Man Micawber laughs. “Lord Brubaker liked ‘is dancin’ he did so he ‘ad the workmen what built the tunnel to the waterfall add in this clever lil mechanism what only works if yous dances near it. Try it, lass. See for yourself.”

Dead End
EXITS: SOUTH

SCORE 260/283; TURNS TAKEN 1315
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 31/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 13/14
________________________________The mine shaft reaches an abrupt end here, where it looks like the ceiling has collapsed. Rail tracks lead into the fallen stone but do not appear again. > Talk to Kristina
Kristina spins around nervously as she sees you there, gives a cry of, "back off, or else you're for it!" but instead of snatching up the crowbar you can see by her feet, she instead grabs a roll of bread and brandishes it at you with a shaky hand.

"Steady with that roll of bread," you say. "It looks nasty."

She glances at the roll of bread, mutters, "oh, for crying out loud-", tosses it down and makes a grab for the crowbar instead, but stumbles over her own feet, falls down, and knocks herself out on the floor.

Well, that was unexpected. If you hadn't just witnessed it, you're not sure you'd have believed it.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 261.

> Get crowbar
You pick up the crowbar.

> Get bread
You pick up the roll of bread.

> Eat bread
You scoff it down, deciding that it's always a good idea to keep your strength up as you'll never know when you'll need it.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 262.

> Wake Kristina
You nudge Kristina and her eyes flicker then open… and go wide as she sees you looming over her with the crowbar in your hands! (You weren't really intending to bash her with it but it certainly helps that you thought to pick it up before waking her up.)

"Blimey!" she gasps. "Sylvia said you were dangerous!"

You wave the crowbar in what you hope is a menacing way. "Are you going to answer my questions?"

Her eyes go to the crowbar then back to you. She gives a brief nod. "Uh yeah…"

You could ask her about her dealings with Lady Montrose, with Lord Montrose, her part in the murder, what Silas's part in all of this, or anything else you like.

> Ask Kristina about Silas
"Oh, he was only too happy to help. He'd been having problems with Joves for a long time on account of Joves expecting him to show up for work and do his job just because he gets paid to do it and I know Joves had been speaking to Lord Montrose about firing him. He came aboard on the condition that we killed Montrose and framed Joves for it, only Sylvia said that wouldn't work because her husband and Joves had been firm friends for years and no one would ever believe that Joves had had a hand in it. That’s why we went with framing Evan. Silas never liked him much anyway and if Joves was off limits, Evan would do and he's dim enough that he wouldn't have a clue what was going on until it was too late. Hey! Don't give me that disappointed look, miss. I had my reasons! Lots of them. I was going to be rich! That was the plan anyway.”

> Ask Kristina about plan
“Oh it all went wrong. And it’s all your fault. Sylvia said we should try and recruit you to help because she recognised a fellow gold digger and thought you could be useful but Silas didn’t trust you. Also because I think he’s a bit in love with her and didn’t want to risk her running off with you instead.”

You and Sylvia Montrose? Well, she’s filthy rich and beautiful to boot which is always a good thing but she’s also involved in a plot to murder her last partner which is definitely bad… no, you think you’re better off with Lord Whatever. Horrible moustache aside, you see him as the better choice. He's definitely way too boring to ever be involved in a conspiracy to have you killed, for starters.

“Only now it’s all going wrong,” Kristina goes on. “We framed Evan but the one straight cop on the force got involved and freed him and now Sylvia says we have to run. Silas wants to stay and frame someone else but I think it’s way too risky.” She rummages in her pocket and brings out a notebook which she pushes into your hands. "Here, take this. It's Silas'. It talks about the plan. I think he kept it because he always figured Sylvia might try and double cross him at some point. But it also shows that I didn't really have anything to do with the murder. Read it. Please. And in the meantime, give me a headstart to get away, okay? I didn't stab anyone. Sylvia will be okay 'cos she's filthy rich and money can buy you lawyers, Silas will be fine hanging out in his lair, but I'm on my own. What chance have I got?"

Sometimes, you reflect, life is just really hard for people involved in plots to murder.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 263.

> Read notebook
The first few pages are certainly an eye-opener, though definitely not in a good way. Someone - you're guessing Silas - talks about his feelings for Lady Montrose and draws some pictures of her. Arty pictures you might call them. With very few clothes included. But with whipped cream and berries aplenty. Oh boy.

But it gets better after that. Silas, obviously figuring that no one would ever read this notebook, or simply being the complete idiot that you suspect him of being, sets out the plan in minute detail. It's basically a signed confession. You're not sure whether this proves Lady Montrose's involvement in the murder of her husband, but it certainly proves Silas'. With this, you could show Pinkerton who is behind Lord Montrose's murder and put this whole matter behind you. You could be married to Lord Whatever and spending his money in a week's time!

Your score has increased by 3 points to 266.

> S
"I'm outta here," says Kristina. "Remember - I helped."

She sets off at a dead run which is ridiculously fast. Even back in your days as a world class sprinter (footnote 14), you wouldn't have been able to catch her.

Your score has increased by 2 points to 268.

Silas' Lair
EXITS: SOUTHEAST

SCORE 269/283; TURNS TAKEN 1342
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 32/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 14/14
________________________________No, that isn't the name you'd have given this place, but instead the name someone has written on a sign jammed into a crack in the wall. The 'lair' consists of a scruffy sleeping bag (yes, it's seen better years, unless it was designed to be tatty on purpose), a stack of old novels and a large amount of dust (though to be fair this was unlikely to have been a design choice but more the kind of thing that just happens). An ancient piece of scaffolding props up one wall, and you just hope it's a lot sturdier than it looks, because if it gives way you'll probably end up buried.  Silas is here.

Silas looks up as you enter his lair, a knife in his hand. "You! I knew we shouldn't trust you!"

"It's all over, Silas," you say, not liking the look of that knife one little bit. Yes, he's an idiot, but that knife is still sharp. "Do you want to come quietly?"

He snorts. "You were a gold digger at heart and didn't believe in what we were doing. We should never have let you into our plans. Now, you back off if you know what's good for you, lady. Take another step and you'll get six inches of cold steel!"

"I don't suppose you fancy surrendering now it's all over?" you ask, a little nervous to be so close to that very sharp knife.

"Never," he says with the zeal of the true believer, "I'll fight to the death." He grins. "Yours preferably."

> Kick scaffolding
As Silas and his knife get ever closer, you kick out as hard as you can... not at Silas, but at the scaffolding. Which shakes, wobbles, creaks... and then settles itself without collapsing on top of him.

"Ha!" Silas sneers. "Nice try, moron. But that scaffolding is sturdy enough to withstand one scrawny, malnourished runt kick-"

And with that, the scaffolding collapses with a thunderous crash, burying Silas beneath it. This causes a huge cloud of dust to billow into the air and quite drowns out your victory cry of "ha! Sucks to be you!" (might need some work doing on your victory cry when you write your memoires). You check that Silas is still alive - he is, albeit somewhat squashed - which is a relief because the first murder of the day has already caused you enough problems as it is without adding another to it.

All in all, you think that went quite well. Clearly the so-called 'instructor' who told you that you'd never make it as a demolition expert had never expected your work on this scaffolding.

Your score has increased by 3 points to 271.

> Examine Silas
He's still alive but a bit on the squashed side due to the weight of the scaffolding on top of him. As he's unconscious and unable to stop you, you quickly search him. (Hey - kicking a man when he's down is your kind of thing.) Aside from an unpleasant amount of sweat and some very questionable body odour, you find some train tickets in his pocket. As he won't be needing them where he's going (his very own room at HMP Prison), you take them.

Your score has increased by 1 point to 272.

> Examine tickets
By the look of it, these are tickets for today for two people to travel from King's Cross. Is this how Lady Montrose and Silas were planning to flee? You think you should show these to Pinkerton. Maybe he'll even let you watch as Lady Montrose is handcuffed and manhandled by his cronies.

Then again, something about the tickets strikes you as suspicious. Why would Silas have them? Surely Lady Montrose would keep them close to hand if she needed to flee at a moment's notice. She wouldn't simply entrust them to Silas. Maybe you should Joves about the tickets and see what his take on it is. He's probably back in his office by now.

Parking Lot
EXITS: EAST, NORTHWEST, SOUTHEAST

SCORE 273/283; TURNS TAKEN 1363
TIMES ASKED FOR HELP 0; FORMER PROFESSIONS UNMASKED 33/33; FOOTNOTES FOUND 14/14
________________________________This is a small, somewhat cramped area nestled between the mansion to the north and a guest house to the east. > Examine cars
One of the cars draws your attention. As well it should. In a parking lot full of police cars and very expensive top-of-the-range vehicles, this battered little Skoda sticks out like a sore thumb. The fact that it has someone dressed in bright pink crouched at the side of it also doesn't help. She sees you at the same time and her beautiful face suddenly sports a very ugly scowl as she stands up straight.

"Hello, Sylvia," you say. "Fancy seeing you here."

She looks around, perhaps hoping she might have a potential ally lurking close by. "I take it Silas isn't coming then?"

You shrug. "He's having a little sleep."

She scowls some more. For a moment, she looks almost ugly. Almost. "Damn you! You ruined everything! I was going to kill that good-for-nothing cheating swine and no one would ever guess I was behind it. Not me, the silly pink-obsessed air-head. But you went and ruined it! Why, I've a good mind to- ow!!!"

"And I," you say, as you drive your knee into her groin with a very audible crunching sound, "have never been one to fight fair." Then you slam your head into hers. Hard. "Or give my opponent the chance to recover." As she crumples up, you deliver a particularly nasty elbow slam to her stomach. "Or lose when I'm this close to winning."

You give her chance to make a witty comeback, but as she's out cold, and making a bloody mess on the ground, nothing much is forthcoming.

Your score has increased by 10 points to 273.

(Press any key to continue)

Pinkerton looks up in surprise as you lead a somewhat battered, though still frustratingly beautiful, Lady Montrose into his office. (Seriously, if you knew she'd still look this good, you'd have probably put the boot in a few more times before you brought her here.)

"Officer," you say, "I've brought you a killer. Feel free to question her at length. She won't deny it," you add with a look at Lady Montrose, "if she knows what's good for her."

Pinkerton gives her a long look. (Strictly speaking, a much longer look than is really necessary but he is a man after all and she, even after several rounds with your fist, is still her.) "Lady Montrose, is this true?"

Lady Montrose looks very tempted to deny anything and perhaps throw herself on Pinkerton's mercy, but after a hard look from you, and your fists, she shakes her head sadly. "It's all true, officer. This harlot beat me without mercy until I was ready to confess. I conspired with Silas to kill my husband."

"And what did Silas get out of it?"

"Well… me, of course."

Pinkerton nods as if to say 'good choice'. He rises to his feet with a pair of handcuffs at the ready. "In that case, Sylvia Montrose, you're under arrest for the murder of your husband. I'm going to see you charged to the full extent of the law and you'll be old and grey when you get released. Although," he adds, "if you're free after that…"

Lady Montrose stifles a yawn. "Oh, please, officer. I might be facing a life in prison but even I have some standards. You’re not even rich."

"In that case, ma'am, you're nicked."

And the rest, as they say, is history.

(Press any key to continue)

You marry Lord Whatever in a glorious ceremony in the south of France attended by friends and family of the groom. Your own friends and family? Not so much. Your mother finds out about the ceremony and decides to attend despite your best endeavours, but a last minute bribe persuades her to rethink her ideas. Your father is thankfully absent, but as he's been absent for most of your life, this is to be expected. The only person who attends that you know is Talia Swayne, all glaring eyes and evil looks, and she spends the day dancing with the richest eligible bachelors she can find, hoping no doubt to bag herself her very own Lord Whatever. You feel like you should really warn potential victims about her, but reason that she might warn Lord Whatever about you, so instead you stay quiet. You just keep a close eye on her all the same.

And you? A weird thing happens: you begin to develop feelings for Lord Whatever. It's not love, nothing that dramatic, but you start feeling fond about him. He doesn't seem half as boring as when you first met him, and while marriage to him is a fate worse than death, and his moustache is as hideous as ever, he starts to seem…kind of…okay to you. Sort of. Your plans to steal all his money and divorce him at the earliest opportunity keep getting delayed and while you tell yourself you're just playing for time so it doesn't seem that you were only after him for his money when you do eventually dump him, part of you starts to enjoy the attention he pays you. Then you get pregnant with Lord Whatever's child, which was definitely not part of your plans… and find, bizarrely, that you're actually happy about it. You're pregnant and happy about it! How weird is that? Morning sickness isn't fun and the wailing brat you find yourself with afterwards… ah, who are you kidding? You love the little menace. You even daydream about teaching her to hotwire cars and crack safes when she gets a little older.

At this point, there's no denying the truth any longer: you're with Lord Whatever for the long term and that's a good thing in your mind. You might have set out to find yourself a rich husband to divorce as soon as you could and steal his fortune, but you went and bagged one you actually liked and now you're set for life. That's hardly the ending you imagined for yourself but, damnit, it's the best one you're likely to get. Give yourself a pat on the back. You've won.

And so you've reached the end of the game. Did you win? Did you lose? And, more importantly, how well did you do? Well, you solved the murder (+10 points right there) which was the main aim of the game so good for you.

Along the way, you discovered 33 of your former professions out of a grand total of 33. That's all of them. Give yourself a pat on the back for this sterling effort. Oh, and if some rather large men come knocking on your door later on to 'have a little word' with you about cheating… well, I'm sure you've nothing to worry about, have you?
